O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, most holy sons, I have completed this book that is the end of the science of medicine, and I have filled it with its contents, and I have made the end by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is distorted in all things, therefore it has perished the science and has been lost, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the vanity, and the minds are closed and the knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive this treatment along with the order of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing instruments, and other tools of the work with the aid of declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters into this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of all, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and rest of them, and the source of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hippocrates says that with the hand alone it is not much, and with work it is little; and equally in the art of manual labor.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that those who are not familiar with the things mentioned before, if they attempt to practice without knowledge and cause harm to men; so I have often seen many of those who meddle in this science and abandon their science and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish woman who cut out an abscess of scrofula or breast of a woman, and cut the arteries of the breast; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another case that treats a stone from a man's eye, and the stone was large; it took with it a piece of the bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for the extraction, and saw the position of the injury and the size of the stone, and if it was cut, it would have died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case that took in care the Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaker he got a wound; and the doctor restrained the fracture above the wound with stitches for a long time, and did not let the wound drain, and so it ended thus; and he commanded that it not be removed; and so it remained until the leg was completely infected and the foot and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and he urged me to come to dislocate his leg; and when I heard it was dislocated, it was in a place and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of the corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another way that crushed the abscess and became putrid, and then inflamed due to the evil of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For putridity, when it is free from melancholic humor, does not need more than to be touched by iron if it is in a place where one can completely remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	Therefore, very dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: first, where there is fear and danger in many positions; and I will show in each chapter of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is important that you keep this in mind, so that the wicked do not speak evil of you if you take up your arms firmly and courageously, and use the best means so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be saved; and let go of diseases that cause great suffering; and remove the weapons that cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of a very ill patient unless you are called a foolish one.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatment into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and non-fire medical cautery, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the irons for cauterizing, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and incising, and about wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell the quality of the help and new harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and new harm is the longest speech and most subtle science and hidden secrets; and for this reason many wise men spoke about it and agreed to it; and I do not speak much about it because I lengthen it.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally in every condition where there is matter, whether the condition is hot with matter or dry without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry weather, they all agreed that the fire cautery is a great help; but others said the opposite, that the fire cautery is only helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the natural heat of fire is hot, and should not be cured with heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite claimed that the fire cautery helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that come from the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the heat of fire, you will see that the body is hot.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no one interferes with it except those who have experienced it, and who know from long experience the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the symptoms and space of time; other constitutions we do not fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the symptoms gathered and agreed on the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my children, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater good than cauterization with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fever is simple, and does not come more than to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members if not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fiery medicines come from one member to another by distancing, and bring diseases of the sick member; and by chance it happens that the evil one fever for its high price and because of the goodness of its substance does not harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put in the art, and it has been above the truth of things; and because I excuse the length of speech, for I do not like to give you the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it breaks diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made in what degree the cautery should be done, and they ask for it.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is beneficial in all cases, because the harm that comes from it is removed by the help of the cautery; and indeed if the cautery is for necessary pain, other than that which cannot wait until the greatest harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as the foolish people do; for to the disease that is healed by cautery there is no return; and they say so because it is not exactly as they think, because cauteries are only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is better medicine for its immediate effect, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the only thing that is good is that the disease comes at a time when the body and its condition are strong; and they are gathered in it the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless you cauterize them in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizing with dense for the pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine, and it is seen; but they do not believe that cauterizing is valid after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterizing is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is well known that cauterization is one of the main methods of medicine, not according to the intention of misguided people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cauterizing instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they only said further that because of the quality of gold and the purity of its substance; and they said that the wounds of cautery do not fester, but I have found that this is not true, as I have experienced, and I have found that it is different in some people; and a gold cauterizing instrument is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And when you heat an instrument of gold, you should not be too concerned about its color turning yellow, and it has already somewhat cooled; and if it is heated too much, then they put it in the fire; and thus it has enough precaution.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cauterization that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter on the shoulder joints to be written separately, for it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is useful for moisture and cold above the skull, and it is done for two reasons: due to a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the shoulder joints, and to the ears, and because of many dreams and toothache and throat pain, and indeed for all diseases that come from cold as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the hairs should be removed by a solvent medicine, changing the skin III or IV times, according to the virtues and the age and the custom of the hair, as much as it can suffer; and then repeat the skin of the hair.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place the cross between your hands, and put your hands on top of it; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his nail between his two eyes; and when you see blood coming out, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", from which this form is:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the bone in its socket with ink, and gradually pull and hold your hand gently in restoring; then remove your hand slowly, and reward the limb if you see the bone slightly; and if you do not see it, start the cauterization again until you see the bone as I have told you; after take a little cotton, and put it in awe and soft cotton inside, and place on the limb, and leave it for three hours; after put a moist cloth on burning; and leave it until the wound is healed; then care for the wound called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said, that the longer one keeps the wound open, the more it purges; and for this reason, it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these say that one should cool the cauterizer so much that a part of the bone is burned, and then reopen what has been burned from the bone, and be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others say that one should cool the cauterizer so much above, and if one removes a piece of bone as wide as the spindle that women put in their hair to let out the humors, and then keep the wound open for a long time; afterwards, one must cure and suture.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to be good in all cases, unless in some people where there is a view of fear; and I think that I should leave it; for the affected person is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and indeed when the affected part is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is safer and milder for me, and of this use I work in such cases.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all cases the main pain comes from chronic pain that lasts a long time, one should use remedies such as years and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head and eyes and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have previously mentioned, it is not good.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	If the patient is of strong constitution and not too cold, then cauterize with that fire which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the head to the bone as we have mentioned before, and cauterize with the vessel which is called "vasselz"; and place it in the place where one puts suctions; and raise your hand so that you do not see jusc’a l’os: the pain from this cauterization is much greater than others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than that with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	when in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease extends to the ear, and the patient is purged by medicines that change the body, and other cures have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and nothing helps: then you must cauterize according to two methods, that is with a hot or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	if the cauterization with medicine is that you grasp a small piece of iron, and remove the skin and coat it with a little bit of the patient's blood, and then make a temple or where the pain is located in such a way that you can replace the piece of iron outside the skin; and when it is replaced, hold and secure it well and leave it for twelve hours; then remove it and treat further with a poultice of bread, and leave the wound for two or three days; then put on a soft cloth dipped in boiling water.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of burns until they are healed; and if you see that some medicines cause blisters, which I have written or prescribed to treat such medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizing iron in this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a clove or it has a little hook, and in the middle a small appearance; and put it on the painful part, and hold your hand and gently press the iron until half of the surface is burned; then lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and bleeds abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on a silk thread and putting it on the limb for three days; then applying a poultice of bread crumbs, and treating the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", apply it at the point, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the wound as we have previously described in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned does not cause much pain and does not suffocate the patient, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is cool; and then apply it to the limb, one line of half a finger's length from the bone, and with your hand take it once, and make sure you do not cover the artery and that it does not come into contact with the bone; and be careful of the mandible which moves when turned, and the nerves should only have regard to the movement and that spasm does not cause pain, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if it is cut with great fear and immediately to the one who does not know, and who has not experienced; and leave the work in this way; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this fire cauterization does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it at the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or from the chapter of extraction of the artery, with the cauterization that has two knives; and this fire cauterization is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes in the ear from cold, and remedies have been applied and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then warm this cauterization called "puncture", of which is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After carefully removing all the skin around the ear, where the pain is felt on both sides, and then move away a little from the base of the ear, as you have marked the point of entry; and apply X punctures around each ear; after healing the ear until it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with caution is no more than those that move from the mouth, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar things that come from scarring and spitting of blood.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you care for this similar torture that moves from a stream of tears and mucus from the chief and gargling, and it does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the pain with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a little later the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips; and put the cauterizer in the part that opens healthy, and make the cauterizer on the chief of the ear above a little bit outside the horn of the chief, and another in the temple as long as a pin; and leave the cauterizer so much up that half of the courage is burned; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the cauterizing knife that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary that the knife be a bit larger; afterward, treat the wound as I have previously said, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauterizations: two on each of the two corners of the head, one on the forehead, and one on the part called "vasselz" as we have previously said, and the back cauterization is on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of laziness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large and modified brain pills; then remove the main part of the disease, and place the sinapi emplaister on the occipital [back of the head], which is written or treated with emplaisters; and this is the way of the cauterization: if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is thus healthy, good; and if not, make three cauterizations of the emis [veins] at the head in descending just above the collarbone, and space one and a half [inches] between each cauterization; and the cure as with the others, and if you have seen to place, and the diseases are suffering, make one cauterization in the middle; and if the work is, two more on the two horns, and the cure until it is healthy; and let the cauterizations called "olivare", as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head of years and of the sweat that we have previously mentioned; after that, rub the head of the painful joint, then make a fire cautery on the head and under each horn, and behind and three times on the spine of the neck; and if you have more trouble, and the skin is wet and the pain is intense, and the disease is not healed, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the worst is over, and remove your hand; after the treatment until it is healed, and let the cauteries that are called «olivare» be as we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization except for those that are fleamatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the pains are great and suffering from lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear the pain, give them gargling and chewing, modifying the brain often with good meat; then give them the medicine in the middle of the head, and do the cauterization according to what we have said before, and the cauterization on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the pains are far and suffering, give them cauteries as I have said to those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is intense, then perform the delicate cauterization as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is causing a large flux, then use the pointed cauteries as we have said for those who are paralyzed.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is declining towards melancholy, and the blood is watery with pain, then give something to drink that cleans the brain, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After relieving the pain of the shoulder; after making a good bandage, like a circle, and placing it on the shoulder; and if the pains subside, and are held well from all sides; then present the liniment, and use old beeswax; and heat it gently in fire, so that the patient can bear it; after emptying the circle from inside placed on the shoulder, and let it cool; and do this for the shoulder once a week with different governance good until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	When you see the fire cautery, make pricks all around the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the brain excessively; and then place on it moistened cotton in lard and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes'
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give to drink the remedy cleansing the head, and keeping it from all moisture, and let it sweat or bathe several times a day empty.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that command him to turn his head, and apply the cautery on the head, and give him two cauteries on the two temples simultaneously, or in one; and cover all the cautery with the veins and arteries that are outside the skull, and so is the cautery long according to the width of the temple; and keep from bleeding of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a cloth.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions, how you should do it; and never burn or cauterize anything outside the two lower bones.
dou cors des larmes	the course of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins, or below the arteries that appear to be in the appearance of the main, and it is seen that it is superfluous cold fluid, then the cauterizing agent that I mentioned at the beginning of the work should be applied: one cautery on the forehead, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations outside the two lower bones; and if there is more, then the sagely cauterizes above the sore with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through the path of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not improve, then drink three bad-tasting concoctions; after that, apply heat to the head, and cauterize or cauterize with the cautery of the chapter; and make two cautery burns called «clavilis» on the two sinews, a little below the ears; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauteries called «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with the cauteries of this cautery called «olivare».
de coi ci est li forme:	of this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you have made two cautery marks as long as the arrows are; and do not leave your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hairs that do not oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is no case where the hairs of the oiled ones are converted to parchment, and they oil, and it is made that cautery is done in two ways: namely by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow long and even, then put the hairs in your hand; after, hold the eyes above the paper of the eyebrows a figure that is as such as the full moon, and be the beginning of the sign above the hairs; then put cotton moistened in oil and musk on the oil, then heat the cauterizing iron:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize on the figure that you have marked a little and little more times, that the curse be in the right place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreating, and the hairs raised to the point of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave thus three hours, then put cotton moistened in butter as long as the burn is healed; after the dressing until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this, the hairs come back, and the paper is softened, then begin the cautery on the same spot again, as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and is even, and do not prick at the hairs with it.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medicine burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of mint; then take French soap and live wax, one of each, and grind them together well; and apply it hotly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the form you have made as the leaf of mint, and put it on the eyes; and if the patient only holds in one eye, then cover both equally; and put cotton wool moistened with oil behind the eye; and let the patient look at the medicine, and press the point and move it every time the patient feels the burning sensation of the medicine, for it feels like a fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blistering is passed, lift the limb up, and reward yourself if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply the medicine again to the limb or the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are fixed; then put on cotton moistened in oil as long as the wounds are chosen, after care the limb of the burn which is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you are uncertain about your work, be careful to stay within the boundaries of your craft, lest you not heal with those tools.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hair prick at the oil, then begin the medicine again on that one which has been softened by the proper paper, as you have done before; after healing, until they are healed; and this is the form of the fume of the mercurous:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the hairs of men are varied in size and smallness, and according to what your constraints may be; and do not reply with the wrong way to that one who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	The care of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head in your hands; and tie the assistant's head between your hands in this way that it does not move, nor moves its head; after put cotton moilliet behind the ear or in the juice of wormwood on the oil; after heat the cauterizer which is there: and it is fastened to the head as if the form of a pen of feather, similarly the one that is the cauterizer; if you see, so it is appointed from the one chief to the other, and if you see, also it is like a tent; but all the same, this which is fastened is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it opens, and in its trace, there is the pus and the dryness; and if it is closed, if it opens, and if it works outside of the bowels; after that, put the cautery very hot, and hold your hand at the part of the neck above the oil, so that your hands do not do foolish things; and put the cautery into the grease of the oil, and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you restart the cautery once more, and if you have experience, and leave it for three days; after that, put soft cotton in butter, and use the desiccating ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without being healed, then put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and the king according to what he would have in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing fistulas that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Apply to the fistula, and clean the area; then put in the fine powder of which this is made:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make in the quantity of a small drop; and hold your hand firmly, and do not move the hairs until the powder melts into its oil; and it is necessary to put on top of the oil on the hair cotton moistened with enough or too much: the powder heals the skin of the fistula, and the wound by a wonderful cure.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the sinus is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer purgatives to the nose, and bring the sinus back to its proper place in the nose as it should be.
des crevaices en levres	mouth sores
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are mouth sores in the lips that are called "poil", and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these sores as we have mentioned in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then one should apply a small cauterizing needle in this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place him in those cracks until he reaches the font; after healing, remove the clay from the limb as soon as it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the bladder, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has fermented and rotted and become old and becomes a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not help much: therefore it is necessary that you have the fire cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula; after breaking or perforating the fistula, and keeping your hand there until the hot iron reaches the font of the limb, and behind the limb; and do so once or twice, then cure as we have said in cures, until it is healthy; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if necessary to reveal the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it does not work, then put a piece of cloth over the bad tooth; after heating the cautery that will come out soon in a certain way that you place a cinnamon on the tooth; and apply the cautery deeply and hold your hand tightly so that the pains feel the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and start the cautery according to your will; after filling the mouth with saltwater, and leave it for an hour and then spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gum softened and held back, and the moisture corrupted dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain from the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness or wind, and medical treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to use cauterization in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a fresh piece, and the end on an iron or brass spoon; afterwards, take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and moisten in hot butter, and put on the painful tooth firmly and hold until it is cooled; and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in hot butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the heated iron until the heat reaches the movement of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauteries are made with fire that is such that you grip a hot iron or brass, and it is thick enough that the smoke does not reach the mouth of the wound; afterwards heat the cautery, because from there will come the form that will be here after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fills its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then let it cool; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cauterization of the wound that you wish, and according to what you have; and it is in the form of a cane:
des scrophules	of sponges
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sponges are cold and humid, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterized wound with the following form, and have two openings for the fumes to issue from the other side; and place the cauterized tool high on the abscess once, or as often as necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cauterized tool according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and place moist cotton with honey on the burn until the wound is healed; afterwards, treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the skull:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overwhelms the channels of the body, and especially when this comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary to first empty the hairs by medicines that dissolve; afterwards, apply cauterization at the root of the throat, and do not bring the heat too close to the throat, but with a little care.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, apply another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the base of the spine, and let the cauteries that are called "clavicles" because of which we have the shape in front; and cure the limb as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the mouth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When tooth and disease of the gums are due to cold moisture, and the pain has no fever or heat, and is an old disease, then apply two cauteries on the forceps in their eyes; and the other cautery goes between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form that is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, apply the cauteries by holding the entire cautery that is called "poins" because of the form that is above in the disease of the ears; and let the poins be just under 30, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, the patient according to what has been said before, and let the fire cauterize at three points in this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the fire cauterizes are lighter, because you make them three times as much.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After, shave the hairs on their back and on their ribs; after, relieve the sore spot inside the tenderness of two fingers of your right hand; and if the joint is misaligned inside, then heat the fire cauterize with two burns in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound as long as it does not pierce through to the other side, and bring together four burns; and because of this, cauterization is made with the three-pronged cautery, for the reason that the shape of cauterization is these three prongs; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the three-pronged cautery.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never place it above this one nerve because it has eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery on top of the wound; after resting the pain, and do not move the member for a long time until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, this matter happens little, then make a cautery above the thick part of the cautery clavicle, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is healed by moisture and is free from pain.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach until it reaches its condition, and they multiply his diarrhea, and are customary ways of cures that he does not profit from, then it is necessary that the pain be soothed above his back, and he extends his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, make three cautery marks with the smallest knife possible due to their quantity, all along the claw, and two more cautery marks after the second rib until the figure of the cautery is at three angles, and have equal space between them so they are not joined together when they bend; and let the cautery be so that it does not press on both sides of the chest, and let the figure of the cautery be in this form without twisting:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the cautery is too large in the stomach according to this form; and if someone is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pinching and holding above the stomach at point i. according to the quantity that you see of it; then cauterize all along the cautery which is called «poins».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the aforementioned cure, as long as they are healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver causes pain from heat and moisture and large vents, as long as it is not removed from its natural condition by excess; and the pains are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help them much, it is necessary that the pains be above its diaphragm; and a sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondres, where the neck of the ox comes; and there should be space between each cautery the breadth of one; and let the cauteries be long as the body, and press not much with the hand at all over the cautery; and let the pain be only on the side, and let the pains be above its feet; and if it cannot, let it lie down, and extend its legs, and lift its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you wish to cauterize these cauteries with a surgical knife, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and you guard that you do not burn all the tissue, for you would harden all the body; and that it does not come close to boiling, for the wounds are very delicate there, and the wise ones should see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the mesh: if it is in the flesh, it does not cause much pain; and if it is in the mesh, it causes intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure has taken effect, if the hairs should grow unevenly on his head; then prick the place where the abscess was, or where there is an aposteme, and then heat the cauterizing iron which is similar to a thorn, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the iron until the pus is all gone; afterwards, according to the treatment of wounds, as long as they are healed; and it should be used by no one except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be boldly attempted, and in all ways it seems to me that it is worth trying.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the fire cauterization
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old said that one should perform fire cauterization with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, and as thick and long as your finger; and moisten it in oil, and place it in the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the eyebrow and the forehead, and two small cauteries a little down in the part that is outside the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the spine, declining a little behind; and one cautery at the bottom, and the other above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the waist, and one between the shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but open it as you would when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And the ancients said that no man uses a cautery like a razor, and they scrape it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and suddenly the pain was gone, as we have said about the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the pain kills now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said about dividing treatments, and it does not improve, then they use three methods of cauterization that are all good.
