Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they would call the ancient "wound healer," and you should make three cuts evenly along the length of the front; one of the cuts as close to the bottom of the front, and the others two at the costal bones above the ribs, and guard against incising the arteries that are above the costal bones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound have a quantity of three drops through the joins; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then plug the opening with the following form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is to be made at the temple just above the second incision; and scrape off all the matter that is between the two cuts as far as the syfac that is above the bone, then make another cut from the other side of the same incision up to the second cut, and then extract this spicule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put in the first cut the tool called "curette", which is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not very sharp, and it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side of the curette towards the charred matter, and the soft side towards the bone, and scrape until it reaches the same cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cover all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is continued up to where it opens, and then make another one in the same place towards the other side; and then extract the arrow evenly, and express the wound for the arrow taken; then put a piece of old cloth in each incision, and put moistened cloths on top made of wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure that abscesses do not come; and the next day remove the bandage, and apply a large amount of fresh sorrel, then the cure of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures that are used to heal wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	remedy for the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any come to have cataract due to custom, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the hair is shaved there is great pain, and the limbs are stiff; therefore, by these accidents that those matters and that cataract do not come only from many wounds, and the cure that is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a deep cut in the front, and another one wide on the side of the neck.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins from the cut on the right temple to the left temple, and the incision should be just above the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move at will; and when the bone is exposed, soak all the blood in a sponge, then wipe between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton, and tents of linen; then bind above with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against suppuration; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to form, then care for things that cause charring, like char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of columbo, and make a poultice; and apply the poultice to these wounds to draw out the char.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earache
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which enters the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or beasts, or stones like iron; or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas; or falling things such as water and other similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it enters the ear as a stone or other hard thing that does not fit well in the ear, it does not grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the arrow, if there is any drop of purple oil or hemlock oil, then apply it to the extraction; and the way to do this is to make the patient spit out the contents of their mouth, and cover their nose when they sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around their ear; and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times the mouth is relieved by this treatment; and if it does not relieve, then apply extraction with fine needles, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps with the needles, it is good; if not, apply extraction with a fine needle of small double-pointed type; and if it does not jump, then make a rain gutter and blow the head of the gutter or the pus from the ear very hard so that nothing can enter with the gutter; then pull it out carefully, because many times it is relieved as we have said; and if it does not relieve in this way, then take some cloth of which they are made, and put something sharp at one end to make a point for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the cloth over the arrow or whatever else, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly cut the ear in the same way as an abscess bursts and comes out, and spasms; and the manner of the cut is that you first make a small incision into the painful part of the ear, and extract the pus according to its strength, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it depends on the fat; and let the cut be like a moon, as far as you come to the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it vigorously into your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a small grain that is embedded and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot be removed, administer the following subtle remedy according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make such incisions when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the acute case when it is in the ear, it is appropriate that the hairs use the first condition of sneezing, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the very ear itself or the sharp one.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the sky, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your hand and light ones, and heat them in the fire; and put the hairs one or punctured of his ear, and go up from his other foot, and strike another stone against the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this stone by stone until the sharp is all out, and thus it jumps all out; and if you see, take the stick, and bore one of the hairs in the ear, and the other head takes fire as long as the least stick is burned; then make other sticks until the sharp is all out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the animal, if it is of small size, as with a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, where one can feel it, then lessen the extraction of pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and where treating distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with delicate pincers, and if they do not come out, then take a needle of this form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And apply the most subtle pressure on the ear according to the amount of pain, then succeed in the whole head; do this often until all the vertebrae are visible.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not comply, then dull the pain around the head with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not succeed as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the opening of the vertebrae, and you will find them where you can treat with distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or of lead is placed at the small pores below, and above over the instrument to distill; and to press within the distillation with a well-made lead tool for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the can, and the can should be in the ear; then blow through the razor all the cotton, and press your hand frequently until the oil is distilled or the smell comes out of the ear; and the bad smell is inside, and the distillation is a little cooled by fire at the same time as it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear deafness
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some sort of deafness in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by deafness from a wound, or from a thorn inside the ear, and this deafness never comes from anything that cannot be seen in the ear, and it never comes from anything else than the deafness itself.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes from inside the ear, if one cannot see it, is from severe infection in many positions, and in this case where one can see, one should put the ear to the bad side in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening entirely of this same space where this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the cauterizing iron be applied equally all around, so that it does not burn the ear; if the opulation is of char cloth or the flesh of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers and gently apply the copper, until that char is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opulation is stuck in the ear, then take a thin razor and gently heat it over the fire, then place it on the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opulation that causes the patient to hear a grating sound, gently perforate it, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent according to the width of the puncture, and moisten it with Egyptian eye salve.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not apply any bandage until the wound is clean, or take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and powder it with broken glass; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is necessary to remove the tent and use another tent moistened with rosewater and beeswax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as soon as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood flows out, soak an sponge and apply cold cloths on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the flow of blood which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the char of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for treating the eyes when they are wet and dry, and you should spread them with forceps and tweezers, and the copper from its roots; then put it on the eye with a solution of sulfur.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without removing it, the cautery of the subtle lens is used, and the cauterizer after the incision is valuable; and many times they are repaired, but nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Frequently in papers come things that seem to be gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail", and it is an assembly of large moisture above and below; the work is such: if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape lightly each part, then take it with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a small hole in the paper, it will not hurt the patient; and if the wound is large, it gathers at an edge, and cure it as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the inflammations restore it soon and heal quickly.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is large and falls into the inner part of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and hold the splinter with some pincers, and press it from one side to the other; and if the paper is moved by incision, it does not hurt anything; and when the splinter is cut, pour oil of strong salt, and cure the limb of which it has injured until the wounds are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is injured in the threads of papers above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes a lot, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears stick to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they are sweaty and sleep on them, and their papers are out of their mouths moist that the exinach inflates in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to your touch and feel the extraneous between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand; and then take a piece of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains extraneous from each part, then place it over it; and press on one side and the other, so that the extraneous is assembled inside the circle; then cut through the moisture at the edge of the wound with a sharp blade, not larger than the wound on the skin of the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the extraneous; and in many positions, extraneous comes from the wound, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove the splinter completely from one piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to push it into the wound, that you do not bring all the oil up to the surface, that you do not damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not appear at the beginning of the wound, lightly rub the wound until it appears; then remove it as we have said, then moisten and dry cloths, and put on the limb, and bandage it well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who bite and put on to corrupt the moisture that is remaining.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the healer comes to the abscess that is not yet healed, then the healer should apply soothing ointments as long as they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When the hairs of the papers are born not natural, and are awake, if they harm the eyes, and bring on various diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and whites, as long as it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in four ways: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine as a cold compress according to what is before or the chapter on cauterization, and is done either by incision and suture or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the pain in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is turned over, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of every thread above; and let it be on the other side of the paper or where the hairs grow beyond these hairs, and take the thread above the paper, and return it to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the skin covered, from the big leg down to the small; then pull the thread, and place outside the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then on top of the paper a figure of an envelope, like the belly of a mushroom, and throughout it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you saw lift the paper which is divided into all.

et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you have skill to cut out a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; then cut all the string on the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the large arm from great to small; and put one of the tears near the natural hairs in the groove of a root, then close the corner into one of the two angles of the key, then scrape the skin; and if not, if you have no care, then leave the seam and the threads for three days or four; then cure the wound without sewing things dry and constricting, because the paper heals at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is dried (as they said the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if in another way: and that you sign the paper in a shape that is as like the figure of a mirror, as we have told, at three points according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then apply this small force evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or if it has a thread, put it in the shape; and put the other thread over the great arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have told you, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with salve and similar soothing ointments; and never once has the hair of the paper been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision, but the sewing on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of dogs is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the needle inside according to what I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the space is; and cope with the two questions of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly above what overhangs the paper of the oil, and strain the two dogs from the two parties form; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the copper has strong forces, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been dressed, and if it was lifted with paper, and they will not grow again; and this is the form of the two cains that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and you insert the silk thread so soft and thin; then assemble the threads and pull both of them subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly, and pull the main thread; then put the hairs on your skin; and let it be beyond the sun so that the work is declined, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle throughout the work in the root of the hair raised, and pierce it into the paper gently until you pull it above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the work, and insert that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out above the work with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the patient is chased and treated, and the hairs do not come out with it, then trace the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes out completely and you see it through the oil; then trace the chase and the thread, and close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and grows on the skin; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the goats naturally, and let it be raised with the one you leave, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the impurity of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "porridge", comes in the oil, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes from wounds, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this is that you break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bind it as long as it is healed; and one should only use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease becomes worse than before; but in the work of things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the root of the sharp or high and seed of linen are cooked, and soothing ointment melted in any of the oils, and there is wrapped a tent, and the treatment of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take heed that it does not decay according to its former form; and this work which we have said is only a guide to this disease, that it does not return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the bone
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the method of the work is that you hold a needle, in which it has double thread, and the thread in the bone, and make it pierce from the left leg to the right, so that the thread comes out in two pieces of the bone; then the bone is held above the entire needle, and the cloth wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper returns to its original shape according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the groove, and turn the paper, and make two cuts within the paper; and let the two cuts of the two angles of the incision you have made meet, and make them into such an angle that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were a letter with no «I greek»; then take that char, according to the quantity that its cost is less than what it would be without paper, then add the two missing parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then care for what we have said about mollifying medicines and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain cut outside of the hairs and papers, as I have said; then drain between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters apply various techniques depending on all possible ways to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the operation and tools in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has been done by many people in a somewhat different manner, such that the paper above is glued with the white of the oil, and it cannot move or do its work naturally, then you should go outside the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too thin, so that the pain cannot bear that the spatula is too sharp or too thin, and makes the oil burn; and your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, should be lightly made, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and that whole assembly is healed, and nothing is ever done in harsh salt oil, and lifted with mild douche, and collodion; then place between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put above the oil moistened wool; and afterwards use douche and remedies as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow joint
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways the elbow joint can be dislocated: one is nervous and resembles a hard, swollen facet, and the other is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, so that when touched with iron and heated with pliers, it cannot be moved; and both start from near the large arm and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and light and movement of the elbow.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the hairs put their head in your hand, then open the eyes; and take the paper to your hand, then bend the elbow with pliers of small double, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or a goat, or a cow, and the thread strong; and double the point of the needle a little and put it into the elbow, and push the whole needle through the elbow, and extend the elbow with a thread and above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that shows the gold and the silk to the hair just above, then cut the remaining in the root of the arm at all the subtle spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision no blood comes out as usual; and once the elbow has been extended only at the end, and the thread, as we have said.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the charred flesh and break it, and that the prickling does not pierce; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk oil, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it just as it is until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the incisions cannot enter, often this appearance of a joint medicine is cured; and they are born as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the oil on the painful spot, and take the spatula lightly with a slightly sharp edge according to this form:

And gently rub the angle above subtly, and if you see that it does not soften and the ratio is approaching, then blow from your mouth into the oil collier made of litargire and red wax and broken silk, and extinguish the oil just after; then proceed with the other work according to this same method until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, such as an abscess, then milk it, and first cure the abscess until it is healed, then proceed with the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is night in the oil due to great harm, then soak it in a solution of one part vinegar and not too much, then pour red wine wormwood into the oil.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the eye that grows above the pupil

But in any case, it is necessary that you apply the cure of each oil weak from the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes' hairs

de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The woman is said to have a "fistula": when you treat it with cauterization and medicine as I have mentioned before, and it does not heal, then you should pierce it at the abscess, where it must die, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then shape all the instrument that is in this form; it is called "rough head", and it should be made of iron as a nail, and pointed as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives. se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is set and the flesh grows, and the body of the wound is sound, it remains like this for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad accidents come, until it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula to the opening of the neck according to this form: and you must uncover the bone the second time with a knife, and with wetting medicines, and when it is uncovered take the foret according to this form, and make the iron of the third angle to the patient as you see above: and let the fistula be attenuated until the top as you see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and does not dislocate again, nor become displaced, then you must bind the pain; then clean it, then place suction cups or hats made of iron to draw out the pus, then place above the eye an ointment made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply the bandage and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity they need; then strain it through a strong cloth, and start suction again without causing pain; then remove the suction and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the eye becomes displaced, you must strain it more; then remove the ointment after the morning and night, and if you see the oil is healing, it is good; if not, start again with the bandage and cloths and ointment and suction until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	forced removal of a burst bladder
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the burst bladder, then open it, and there comes forth a great deal of paper-like substance, like a grain of resin, and it is difficult to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you would stick a needle into the root of the part below this above, then stick another needle or a double thread of the part of the arm; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then cover the thread double and tie a part of the bladder around it, and hold it well, then pull out the needle and put on the oil lotion in abundance of urine; and let it stay until the thread has healed with the bladder, then care for the oil of things that comfort until the wound is healed; and never once the wound is restrained by the bladder from every part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly swollen, pierce them with a fine needle that comes from underneath the oil, and remove the moisture and descend to the eyelids, and enter them immediately; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from beneath the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease that is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a swelling that is gathered in the oil, resembling acute downward, and it is not acute; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit upright and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the mouth until you see the swelling coming up to your eyes; then sew it up, and do not descend and be dismantled in the light, and see the things as they should be; and if it does not descend, it is acute, and if it descends from the swelling, it is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you let the pain rest between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it over the corneal suture and the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal suture and the crown, until the wound is open; and when it is open, then pour hot honey mixed with oil, or honey boiled with fenugreek and honey, then let it be cured by other cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oils of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar oils in the division, and what is needed to pierce; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the hurt part between your hands crossed, outside of the light for the sun, and with the clean oil pressed and strongly stretched; then place the paper of the oil in your right hand if the hairs are on the left, or in your left hand if the hairs are on the right; then take in your right hand if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if the hairs are on the right; then place the point of the instrument above the crown by the thickness of a rat in the part of the oil that is between the big toe and the little toe, then strike the instrument called «almagda» vigorously, and withdraw your hand until it pierces into the part of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the front of the measure of the space that is from the moon to the end of the nail; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then place the instrument above it where the sharp is, then extract one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he is now sharp, he sees the hairs before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, if he is sharp again, raise the second vein, put the sponge with the instrument, and when it is firmly attached and does not rise, gently turn around your hand a little and a little; then put in a small piece of silk, and leave it in the wound.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the oil soaked or linen cloth in rose oil and plenty of honey, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on top with plenty of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the needle cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some people who have very hard eyelids, then you must use the tool called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too far in front, but make the eye subtle, then bolt the hardness, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the patient's sleeping position, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and with all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition for this time; then release him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and see some things, and then return the bandage after seven days; and it does not matter that you do this in the evening of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to raise the eyelid quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply a poultice before the seventh hour, and bring it to the mouth of the wound to drain the pus; and when it is drained, remove the cloth and put on a new one to cover the wound, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then slowly bring it out of the house and return to its place; and heal that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who was of the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people would make all kinds of arrows, where they succeed the sharpness, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read it in any books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of alchemy, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the chief of those from this same subtlety, and the latter in three angles equal.
de la char sor le neis	of the healing of the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No blisters or boils ever arise from the nose, of which there are some that seem like scorpions at the root; and if there are such, or if there is a blister of a good color, and if there is a blister of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those blisters that are of a good color, and not enchanted, it is necessary to place the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the droplet into those blisters, and draw them out; because this corresponds to what you can support in the subtle spirit agitated from one part, until you know that that blister is completely hardened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that can be covered, open it with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you are overcome, or an abscess forms, remove it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the wound is not stained and all the pus is removed, then pour out or cleanse with a solution of salt and vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not heal, and moisture enters the palate, if it is not cleansed, there may be pus in the bone above, because the instruments do not come out well; therefore, it is necessary to bring a piece of linen thread, thick enough to hold with our hands, and space out each nut according to how much or little; and put the bad parts of the thread into the patient's mouth, and pull it through the nose until it comes out of the mouth; many times they do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it; then hold the thread that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other thread that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and clean each one after the other as we do with our fingers.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that they have not corrupted that part of the bone, then remove the son, soak the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian egg yolk, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the eggshells corrode all that remains of the bone; then place a piece of bread under the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, shaped like an open lamp, such as a dog, and bring it thus; and if you see, make a closed dog, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder joint
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Frequently, a disease arises at the shoulder joint, which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time; and for this reason, it is necessary to cover it from the beginning, and to apply the entire bone, then put the fire cautery or the burning medicine on it; and if one delays in covering it until it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and insensitive: if one does not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when one covers it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is softly touched, not with iron, and you see that one can cover it entirely, then remove the pain and cure the limb of similar things and restrain them.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	when solutions of continuity come from one of these cartilages, it is rare and only in some people
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, look to see if the lips are split on both sides; then stitch them together at the seam, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already split on one side and not the other, it is necessary to scorch all the parts that are not yet healed, then gather the two lips together at the seam, hold them in place, and powder with dragon’s blood powder and frankincense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and let it soak through, then treat the wound until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you assemble the needle: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the mouths of people, there are abscesses inside the lips, hard and small, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut under each one, and take out the pus with tweezers and clean every part; then apply the leek after incision of broken glass, until the wound is not soaked; and then apply the oil of eucalyptus, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth's gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, abscesses arise above the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; therefore, you should hold them with forceps, and cut at their root, and let out the pus or blood; then put on the tooth a vitriol powder broken into pieces, or other restrictive and desiccating powders; and if this gum returns after incision, and often does, then cut again, and cauterize: if it does not return after cautery, these are the forms of instruments to cover.
des sordens	of deafnesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, abscesses are assembled at the root of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scars that are ugly and sharp; and sometimes they are black and yellow and green, as far as corruption reaches the gum, and are bad-smelling teeth; therefore, you should put the painful thing between your hands, and its cause in your holy place, and extract the teeth or scars as long as nothing remains; and thus make black and yellow and green, and yellowish and others, until they are all cleaned; and if what is at the first layer is good, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the tool, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth have business with various forms of tools to remove, because the tool used to remove between the teeth has other forms than those used to remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, you should pull the tooth as much as possible, as no one should do this; for it is a substance very high just above us that we have no excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the tooth is painful to pull, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth hurting.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times, the pain of the tooth is relieved, and make sure it is not a bad tooth, and pull the good tooth; and then the pain does not depart, until the evil ones are extracted, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are certain of the tooth hurting, it is necessary that you burn around the tooth in all places; then move it with your fingers or subtle tweezers at the first and second point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly hold the tweezers; and let the one who has the pain in your holy place between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, take one of these instruments and push it lightly into each part, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulp is; and if the extraction is subtly held by roots, that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to cover around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and reapply to the pain by the greater evil of the root more severe pains of the first.
