Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant saint does, who by their haste and boldness break the chariot once and for all, and never bring back what we have told; but bring forth once again through the quackery of this great disease due to the roots that they delay, or due to the chariot that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the density is traversed, wash the limb with wine or oil and salt; and if blood flows out, which often happens, use the limb of vitriol broken; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, by which one moves the first teeth, should be long pointed and large handed, so they do not double up when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large enough so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be shaped to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, it is necessary that you put a soft cotton wool moistened in oil or butter on the tooth.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the tooth is softened, then pull the pliers which are called "algefri", of which the patient resembles a beak; and they should be made inside like a wedge and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not want to come out at all these needles, it is necessary that you dig around the root entirely, and put the tool called "althali", which is a spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too thick so that it does not break immediately, and if the root jumps up through the hole, it is good; if not, if you help with all the tools, of which these shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this tool that has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the range of the teeth, and with this tool that seems like large needles, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is different from others that it cannot break, and sharp that many of the instruments of dense are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of them; and if they break the carriage or other bones, or if it does not help, if they look for the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and help with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and strong to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; then restore the limb to medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not straight along the natural pathway, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, then it is necessary to remove the tooth if it is not in the right position, and it cannot be straightened or filed; then use this tool which has a shape similar to a small beak, and it is made of iron with a sharp edge:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper pounded gently over time due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the copper is shaped like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the shape of the copper from which arrows are made; and in the copper, gently pound the tooth over time, so that it does not move until it breaks; then, at the end, use a file with no roughness at all, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, it must be filed until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front are loose, whether by impact or by falling out, and the pain cannot be relieved because they cannot be held down to prevent them from falling, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, it does not work; then you must bind them with a gold wire, for the silver wire turns green and rots, but the gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are loose, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the injured tooth or teeth in the middle, as many as there are, until you can safely reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin to cover the injured part again, and gently and skillfully tighten your hand until it does not move; and let your thread be attached to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then thread the threads with a wire, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that they do not bite the tongue; then leave them tightly clenched as long as possible, and if they loosen, or the wire breaks, then use another wire; if it holds, it will serve in this way for the entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two missing teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth breaks, if you reset it in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and do not interfere with it until it is wise and painful, and never once is the shape of a cow's bone tooth made, and you put it in the place of the deficiency, and you tighten it as we have said, and hold it so for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of covering the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no joint that comes out of the tongue or by nature, which one is born thus; or by accident of a wound; and the works are such that you open the mouth with the pain, and hold the head in your own, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous part of the large, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or no, and it is by a severe wound, if you beat the one and cover the other loosely; and be careful that the wound does not become too much in front, for the artery which is out; and when you have done, lift the shoulder of high rose and vinegar, or high cold, then put the tongue out of a linen tent; and the pain every night, so that the wounds cannot suppurate.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes out, apply vinegar to the wound; and if it does not stop bleeding, cauterize with slow-burning coal, which is good for the skin; then care for the wound until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the wound is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to suppurate and there is moisture, pour water through a fine sponge, and deliver it from both sides; and if it does not stop bleeding, apply vinegar until it stops. Then remove the bandage and care for other wounds until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of neck abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes from within the neck boils that are called "godath", and they are properly called the II mandibles, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is an abscess hard of small sense and of pus color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, rather for the flow of blood; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check that the abscess does not rest and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the injured part in front of the sun, and its joint should be in its proper position, and the work of the mouth and the spear of the sergeants between his hands, and press the tongue out of all the instrument, from which this is the form; and it should be of silver or thin brass as some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the needle and the cotton in the amber, and the thread above as much as you can; and take nothing from the cloth with it, then cover the instrument with the thread, which resembles a forceps; and everything else is curved, one part the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have a pair of pliers, here is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, it is blunt; and when you have gripped one of the tongs, grip the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the sharp pains with hot, sharp, and soothing water, and if blood comes out, gargle the sharp pains with hot, sliced green apples or mint leaves, and similar things, until the mouth is clean; then cure it as much as possible; and never do any other incisions in the throat except the two tongs, so grip them in the same way as the two tongs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was nestled within her throat, specifically a small abscess; and it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so much so that the woman could not breathe or swallow, and she died if she remained like this for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been filled with two drams of pus through the two pores of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore immediately pierced one incision into the abscess, then through the great wound, and a large portion of blood; then I made another incision into the other pore of the neck, and pressed against her mouth and tongue; after piercing the incision into these abscesses, and taking out a part, and not more than a small amount of pus came out; thus the woman's breathing was relieved from the obstruction in her throat, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscesses kept recapping and filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I pushed and cauterized it from within her throat: thus it did not grow again; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When removing from the eye, and it is infected and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is round and large, it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you should drain it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red or black, then you should avoid incision of the abscess.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	When you see it, according to the method that I have mentioned, of its length and breadth, that you make the hairs sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned before; then put the needle into the wound, and draw out the arrow, and cut it with one or two of the instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you cut off only the excess that is beyond the natural end; for if you cut more, it will cause great pain to the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two arrows, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is intolerable, then it is necessary to use a cauterizing instrument for the sensation of pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of the cauterizing instrument is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your shoulder, and then presses the tongue against the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and applies with sharp and live fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in moving this instrument, it is like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head has a hair or object that puts the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and puts the instrument on all the medicine on the gum; and the patient is lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle drip from the mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and the blood; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the gum for half an hour, until you see the medicine is healing and the effects of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through all the cotton into the cavity above, until the cotton is burned on the gum; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days. And if you have to start the cauterization of the medicine again, start it again, and after the cauterization stitch it around the gum with cotton soaked in honey, and clean what is around the medicine; and be covered with sharp cold, and be treated with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from incision than cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take camomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and add vinegar; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and it should be one of the ends of the instrument inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; after that, it is repeated often, until the eye is dry, and keep in mind that you do not make this at the beginning of the arrival of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this unless at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, take a cloth and place it inside the head with an egg shell, so that the mouth does not have too much heat; for the egg shell does not make much steam to burden the mouth, and this is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is necessary to remove an object from the throat or fish bone, or nothing at all; therefore you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all the instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit the object as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the object is stuck by vomiting; or the object swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the stomach, it will stick, and then pull out the object; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take the instrument from the bottom according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved to the head so that they can more lightly enter the throat, and raise the head high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to him, nor put the bone inward; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, because it is softer or the thing is as such; if the push goes down, or it pulls the instrument throughout equally, until it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's flesh
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the throat's flesh, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not improve, then look at the throat's hair to the sun, then that you press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the sinew, then trace it all with a small needle, or with fine needles that are worth the eye.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth it, then take a hairy cat, and beat the hair of the sore with it, then beat or move the hair of the cat against the iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wound is tainted all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full bucket of cold water, and work the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it to his hand often; and when the sinew soon feels the cold, then stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not sneeze as we have said, then steam the wound with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will eventually clear.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is that you hold a pot with burning charcoal or where it has charcoal, and place the cover over it with a perforated lid in the middle, and in that puncture the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the head of the cat in its mouth, and close its mouth, so that the fume does not escape but enters through the nose; and the nose will now sneeze, and if it does not, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salted things and others, and do not drink anything sharp; and thus it is necessary that she should be cured by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the jaw, so that when one can see it, it resembles a hooked tong depressor to enter the throat; and it has the appearance of a beak, and there is an abrasiveness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot wear out; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and cut; and it is in two ways that one is in its own likeness, and because it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are at the neck.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the chief is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the neck is other than that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is dead according to its completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are crusty, and do not die according to their completion, as abscess which are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscess comes beyond joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by, perhaps because the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located deep within the limb, and if you delay perforation until it has died, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located deep within the foundation, if you pierce it too late, it will not be able to pass through, and will remain long inside, and there comes a fistula; and it cannot be healed in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to remove the head of the perforation of the abscess that has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and inflammation, and the lessening of the debatement and the easing of the main abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation where more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens most; and if the perforation is long in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the limb, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before then, it may cause the vein to bleed heavily, and it is painful due to much feces; and perhaps it hardens the lips and penetrates deeply into him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that are punctured according to the width of the vein, according to what the limb has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you incise small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them with a cloth, and bandage; when they have become as soft as cloth, and are mortified, then it is necessary to do as one does with bubbles: and if there are such abscesses that are cut into three angles, and if there are such that one covers as the fleece of wool, and others cover as abscesses; and if there are such that one makes a round shape, and other shapes and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the wound is superficial, it is necessary to lance it clearly; and if the abscess is large, and there is much pus, and you lance it, do not draw out all the pus in one hour, but take out a part; then stop the abscess on the other side, then take out nothing else; do this gradually, many times, until all the pus is out; specifically if the wound is of weak virtue, or carried by women, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never dare to touch the wound with the discharge of the pus, because by chance the wound may die, and you will not be harmed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small; and if a tailor complains, mend it with linen or wool cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you stuff each one with a tent so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have pulled it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rags of linen against moisture, and tie it just above the wound; then open, and treat the dressing as long as they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flows from your work, apply sharp cold and oily, and wipe the cloth, and put it on the affected area for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood flow persists, apply government and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is very tense or if the wounds are very painful, it is recommended that you put on bandages and clean with wine and oil; and if it is in a swollen state, and the wounds are charred, it is recommended that you put on bandages and clean with cold and oil, or with wine and oil warm, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress and heal, as it should, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the chest, and are like those in cloth, like the lance of a goose, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also some large and such ones that have moisture like fish; and there are some that are hard and rough to cut through, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the belly is that you prove with every tool called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it does so by going through the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off the hair that contains that moisture, for it will stay in place if you leave nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it there until the next day; and this will prevent what remains from sticking.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for its condition until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess is large, then cover it with this form, long; and pour in your ointments, and scrape the skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it lies; and if the artery causes contrary, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this if the abscess is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting above the abscess, if it is more superficial, because it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or swellings have no moisture, and among them were the abscesses I had seen or the swelling of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone tried to cut it, they would make as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or swelling, those that come at the root of the children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent part, to let the pus out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of hiccoughs
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times have there been abscesses at the neck, and they are dislodged with difficulty, and they are painful, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body or chest, and they are very large, and they are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each hiccup is properly within its own side, as with the one and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these hiccups are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malicious and do not wish to obey to health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then that you see of good disposition in the touch, and is similar to the color of the blood, and is mute from every part and is not attached to any nerve, artery, or conduit, and is not deeply set; it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape every part, and let the two lips of the wound come together as they should, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and take out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make it too thin, that the hand does not slip, and do not look too early, before you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to stop bleeding, put in the wound vinegar broth, or some powders that stop bleeding, and stop the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and begin to poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is clean, return to your work, until you complete it; then consult your indicator whether there are any small scabs left, and cut them and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, then it is not necessary to cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through, without causing harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrophule, it is necessary to gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, as there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary to cover the root of it and draw out the forceps, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that have superfluity, pierce the place where it opens to die; and pierce in this way as before mentioned, depending, then apply bandages and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, the cure of bandaging with charcoal until it is healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I have never seen such a person in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the edge of the throat, which is called "epiglottis," be avoided; and this cannot be helped because all the veins and the source of the evil are in those who have abscesses largely in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the source of the veins, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it outside of three circles or four with a small cut through between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the throat, not in the cartilage; and those cuts are convenient for the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the vessels are long and do not bleed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the throat until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the wound as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the windpipe that flows through the bone which is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour is passed when there is doubt of strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause blisters to rise until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this juice so long as the throat is completely stopped up, and the hairs are judged to be dead, and the defect has drained away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore one should cover the epiglottis for this reason that the hairs cannot maintain, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and because they commanded the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stabbed herself in the throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled from the vein except through the throat, and the blood flowed out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sutured the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the young lady did not die because she was called back to life, and returned to her usual condition; for I believe that in the tissue of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in color like jelly, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural or accidental; or naturally without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one occurs in two ways: one is similar to a large abscess, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and it causes fear, and should not be operated on except by a skilled surgeon who is small and experienced: if you find it like the large abscess, and cannot be removed at all, then treat it as you would a large abscess, and cover it with a bandage if there is none; and examine it closely and treat it properly until it is completely healed.
des nous	The fire cautery in
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of us are, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell the difference that is between us and the other.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the other is cold and feverish, as long as the boils have not passed, and is accompanied by the purging; then the fever and cold rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With ours there is neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syphilitic ulcer, which is its own pus and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a small sore, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the care of a new patient, it is necessary to first test and inquire about the use of an instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as it appears in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you hold or press on a moist cloth in the abscess, and return your fingers slowly and gradually, until you know that the instrument has pierced through, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the wound is moist and has a discoloration, treat it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after the incision, there is no more moisture, then scrape it thinly, and then scrape off the skin from every part and remove the flesh where it sticks, and take out the tissue with a clean cloth; and if you cannot take it out cleanly, then tear it off in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if nothing remains, then it returns many times; and if it stays for a short while and does not bother you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and hold the wound, and put on things to calm the abscess, and treat other wounds until it is healed; and if it is large, then cut out both lips of the wound, and treat what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it is contrary to you or another, and you hurry and fill the wound with broken glass, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound heals, and rest the blood clot; then return to cover what was left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the shapes of the probes used for puncturing, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, to search for the abscess of fistula; and they are also like the arrows that one buys the pots with, and are made of yellow gold, or iron, or silver, and are worth as much as those that are already yellow, and are more expensive because of the black plague for searching for the openings of fistula; and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are nails with two claws of three ways; and if there are nails with three claws, and they are also of three ways; and if there are nails with two claws, and a single claw, and they are of three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these that are made are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except in one part, from which we remove the nails, so that they do not cut the vein or the nerve; and these are called awls, which are replaced in needles, so that the patient does not suffer at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses only a small one in the case of a limb that is chapped, such as legs, arms, and breasts, and angles, and similar parts; and never made any other instrument small, like the scrapers of pustules, according to this form, with which we drain blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never placed back in its place which can cope with veins, and arteries, and once again returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, if it is necessary to follow this form of this line .b. until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing char, then stitch together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is greasy like women, then cut into the ribs above, by similar cuts; because one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made completely, because the pains do not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton gauze in a corrosive ointment; and let it remain until it melts the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the ankles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the ankles are ways of hard scrofulous nodes or they have sides, and there are those that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is drained, then apply old cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an ointment suitable for this as long as it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	If the abscess is similar to a scrofula, then treat it as we have said in treating scrofula wounds, and if the wound opens again, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the bursting of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	If the artery bursts and the skin above is hard, then there are often abscesses and also blood in the vein; and if you know it is for the artery, then the abscess is long and pointed; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is firm; and when it is for the vein, it is red and swollen; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and joints and collarbone and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the use of the iron, and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is inflamed by an artery flowing through the long skin; then open the belly with a needle, and pull out the artery as far as it is exposed; then stop it with a double thread of silk, according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not touch the skin between the two strands of the fascia until the pus is removed, and remove the abscess; then treat the wound as directed, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the belly, if you dip your hand in the pus that comes from the abscess to all the skin, then pull out the needle with the thread that you hold in your hand, and poke it through the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, or the thread of one of the two parts of the needle at the incision of the first needle, and if you doubt that the thread will not stick, then take another needle with a full length of thread, and pull it through all the abscess in four strands; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the wound and leave what is attached; then put on a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat the wounds and inflammations until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the neck when it is cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And it often happens more frequently in the assistance and the doubtful cases, and in all of them where there are joints, and this is very bad abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions with pain; and when one stretches it, it causes great pain, and it is not in the same position as the body, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not usually cover them with iron: perhaps they have contraction; and those who are on the head or face, making the skin to the spasm.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if it has a point at its base, and the copper at its root; and if it is large, if it is suspended from its base, and scraped, then the bone, and remove the skin, then the bone and assemble the wound at the seam, and the cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There are no times when they occur in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and large heads; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or three in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were cut open with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the workings in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the arrow is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the cutting often comes too great bleeding of blood, and if you do not see the hair spouting and painful from the incision of the iron, then take the thread of good material, and tie the arrow as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain, and do not cease to stretch the thread of good material until it covers the arrow, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then pour directly onto the belly, but you should well cover the half, then cauterize that it does not return; then care for the wound, and guard that you do not cover the flesh which is of pale color and poor sense and of light look.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these infected abscesses, I will come to treat chancres later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the patient is bound, he should be placed in a dark room.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the blister comes from fire wound or cut of the face, and is above the belly and among some of the blisters, as it has in other wounds, of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of pus; and if it is from the cut of the face and from the outlet of the feces, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.
