And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses at both sides, it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when one presses at the hand, do not constrain too much; and if it is for blood, it opens greatly by these signs of the abscesses, which are thick and hard, and is filled with a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work appears whether it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, it is necessary to command the patient to dye his hair, and be stretched straight all around, then sign all around the belly; then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked with a sharp instrument, then stretch half of the abscess above the large incision; then tie it tightly with a strong silk thread, or a firm rope, and let the intestine rest on it; if you pull the intestine, if you release it, and bring the intestine out through the belly; and if you pull the boil, if you take it at the base, and cut off the excess; and if the artery makes it against you, or the vein, go around slowly, then return to your work and take two needles, and bring two threads of fine silk, and cut the two needles where you have done as you should perforate; then stretch the abscess in four points above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb until it can bear, and kill the dead flesh by itself; or take it when it has become thin and can bear, then cure what is necessary, and cut the abscess as we have said; and strain the blood or moisture that you have taken, then cure the limb as it should be, and wash it.
dou chancre	For the fire cautery, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the workings, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge once the bad from black bile; then make it healthy if it has manifest repletion, then wash the bad out of good blood; then pour your instruments or chancre, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and clean it well with your hand or something, and if the bleeding does not stop, do not make the incision of the artery or vein, if the cauterization is not finished; then treat other wounds until it is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken in the division of the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of the acute is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only eclipsed; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hypo-archy, for it is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called «eclipsed» by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look at whether the evil is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as with all and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the evil of great virtue, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then thus: lean the evil straight up your hands, and press the belly in lifting the acute to the lowest part of the bottom, then take the spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be cutting from two parts, at the tip, and no part should be so thin that it can come into contact with the intestines when it is cut, and it cannot be bleached; then look if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if it is necessary to cut off three fingers' breadth from the left side of the belly III dois; and if it is for the disease of the liver, then the cut should be on the right side of the belly III dois; and if it is for the mucus, then it should be on the left, and it is not necessary that the hairs grow over the cut so that the superfluous ones do not run to the weakest limb; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and squeeze, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the flesh as in scraping at the quantity of an angle or around; then pierce the flesh until the space comes to the desired length, and this is the length of the scar, then remove it, and if you squeeze this instrument with the form:

Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever born who does not have a hernia in the staff, or the hernia is small, or it is not in its place.

des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife

de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not of the same kind as other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly in children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the greatest part of the masters and the wise who performed circumcision in the Middle East, and among the forces, and all at once; if it were up to me, it would be two threads, and by chance if one covers the other and delays the other.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut. De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound dressing that is done with force to all the length of the thread, I have found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut equally as well above as below.

dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to the blockage of a stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or charred meat, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone that is high or at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the pain be pulled up over his knees; and his feet are placed on his back, and his abdomen is extended from the part above the back, and he is strained as much as possible; and then the neck of the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called «siringue», which is made of fine silver hair, like the pen of an eagle; and its tail is a palm long and half, and it is thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the linen or cotton to the pouch, and push the head of the thread into the tube; then fold the excess linen and push it towards the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on the seat, and the bladder and the wet cloth of oil and olive oil and vinegar; then place the tube heavily in the cloth, until it reaches the root of the cloth, then double the cloth over towards the top; then push the tube forward just before the bladder, and the patient feels the urine coming out, and it is not made according to this order except for those who are turned or go there; then tie the thread all around the pouch little by little, and the urine follows the linen, then remove it, and correct the urine; and repeat the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When pus or blood comes into the bladder, and putrefaction is present, and you see it drip watery and medicinal substances, then use all the instrument called «clepsedre», and it is this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the needles are passed through the place where the medicine courts so that it stops well the urethra without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and put when necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and pull to the drawing which is inside; if you draw the moisture to the syringe, and then strongly push the drawing inside; the moisture will enter inside, and it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheterizes the bladder: if it is in:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of lead, and it is the highest; and remove it from the side where the veins lie; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see cluttered in the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed by a good quality thread doubled, and heat the moisture over the fire; then pour the head of the poultice into the rod, then hold your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then tie the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the bread, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in rain, and all signs, and in which stone one should open a hole; and in the bladder, and in the rod; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone embedded in the bladder is more common in children, and it is a sign that the sharp jump of the bladder resembles a sharp jump in its subtlety; and there is hair, and great pain in the rod, and it happens many times, and then it returns; and at most of these jumps the foundation; and it is light the healing of children up to they have IV years, and it is very difficult for elders, and it is as constant as those who are between young and old; and it is a lighter cure for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it towards the outside, so that the stone descends to the edge of the anus, and does not pass out of the thigh; then place it between your hands prepared, and your hands are away from your thighs, so that the intestines are all descending below; then take and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If she does not bleed at the touch of the finger, if your index finger of your right hand is greased, if the pain is sharp, or if your middle finger is greased, if the pain is dull; and place it on its base, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the neck of the bladder; then press upwards at your finger, and the stone where you see it was cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand over the testicles, and his left hand to remove the skin on the side where the incision is made; then cut the spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere. A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins where it should be cut, make the incision wider; and if it does not fit, it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping; or you can use a subtle hooked instrument at the head; and if you cannot engage it in this way, enlarge the hole slightly, and if there is no bone, then strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the smaller ones, and if there are many more, do so afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be cut larger, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor. Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, apply moss and vinegar to the dislocated joint, then use a healing ointment and basilicon until it is healed.

And if an abscess comes to the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is retained by the urine, which is known as a sort of torture: then apply your remedy to the wound, and extract that clot, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and ruin it; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and silk, and assist in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you apply, that you tie the two thighs together, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the arrow is small, and it is conveyed with a stick, and tied tightly, and the urine cannot come out; then the cure for this that I have said before, that you should cut many times, is to excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and be at three angles tied with one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the arrow around the rod outside the wound, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then lightly beat the iron rod on the thread until it reaches the arrow; and gradually turn the iron rod in your hand into the arrow until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; if urine comes out immediately, then press your hand over where the remaining part of the arrow is inside the rod.

de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is rarely a stone in women, and if it ever happens, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who will expose herself willingly, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the woman's stone is further forward than the man's, because it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, you should summon a skilled midwife, and if you do not have one, do not proceed with the operation; and present a clean blade in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command for the examination of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is virgin: therefore, it is necessary to put her on her back and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she should push it out of her body, and recommend that she push it out or with pain, and press her right hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary to move it from great to great, from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the body, where it is most likely to be found, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her above the stone or below, and let the tailor make a small opening in the belly, if you feel the stone so sharp that the wound cannot be closed until the stone can be removed, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those that rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, put leprous vinegar on the wound, and keep it there for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work, until the stone is fully formed, and have the tools that I told you about in the extraction of the stone to help you in your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and bandages and ointments, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for fear that the patient might die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limb has healed, then return to your work, until the stone is fully formed.
de hernie carnouse	of a cancerous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Water hernia is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white feces, which is outside the intestines, which contain the urine; and it is called "syfac", and never properly in the tissue of the urine, if one considers that it is another urine; and this is the skin of the intestine between the white feces that we have said; and it does not have a pole.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is due to weakness that comes from the womb, and it is spread out with that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from the blows on the womb, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a declining color to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and there are more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, for if it is white and facial as we have said, then it is the abscesses that we have mentioned, not long like an egg, and does not open the womb, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own egg, then it is the abscesses that we have mentioned with part of an egg, and because one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the womb and the white facial as we have said, then it feels good; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the surrounding parts, for that is how it was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to as much power and the replenishment of its body; then place it on its back, on something a little high, and cover it with much cloth; then bend over its right side, and command the minister that he bends over the left, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the chest; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the ribs from long to above the knuckle, and let your stroke be straight in dividing the skin of the ribs to the white fat, and scrape the skin subtly according to as much power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp edge from wide to large through the hole, and extract all the sharp, and then put your forceps, and close the white face above; and do not touch the chest except the white face itself; scrape all or in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, if you do not scrape it well enough, it will return to the sharp; and if the wound opens again to your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white face; then gather the two flaps of the chest at one seam, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit. de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	There are many different situations in this section of this branch that seem to me to be worth leaving, and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from wounds and immediately to the groin; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive sharp and cold, which is spread in the groin, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is like the color of the blood; and it does not have any pain, and it is a painful abscess; and perhaps it is some gray and putrid abscesses, and of yellowish color, and sometimes comes from a wound of an artery, or from an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the appearance of an abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their appearance at the touch of your fingers, and can often make the incision above this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you should cover the wound with the corresponding part, then place the end in the top, and the thread from the white silk face, and deliver the suspended part from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already healed with these charges, then it should be incised, and covered; and if it is in the face, or inside the vessels, then it should be delivered entirely, and covered roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the head of the shoulder is born behind the back, it is necessary that you cover it entirely, and straighten the neck, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then perform other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bandage, with the softening of the groin, and the patient cries out in pain when moving; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the dislocated joint sit on the seat of the shoulder, then lift the suspensory ligament of the ribs to your fingers, and all the tendons that are close to the thigh, and tie the master muscles, and extend them evenly; then cut with a sharp knife across the tendon in the middle, as far as they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples; then take an needle or double thread, and tie it to the first bone where the blood came from, and tie it to the other end; then suture in the middle correctly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted blood; then treat the wound as with others or when one is bled, so that no vein is cut that belongs to the ribs; for by this there is no harm, and if all the veins come out of sight, it is necessary to remove the ribs from all the veins; so that the bone does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the veins, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are from the section that comes out or the extension over the belly in the part of the ankles, because the intestines descend from that toothache to one of the joints; and this toothache is either from the section of it, or from its extension, and these two methods of many causes come: from the shock, or the jump, or the shout, or the lifting of heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it comes to the extension of the toothache, it is that it is painful and painful in a long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal up to the front, because the toothache approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the appendix, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and has various abscess appearances outside the skin, and is for the outcome of the intestine and the body due to the appendix.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the bowels are not sent with the intestine, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of fear of iron, because it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or make the patient roll up the intestine with his hand inside the wound, if it can be inserted; then place the head above between your hands, and relieve the ribs; then the chest is held above, and cover all the skin of the belly; then put one finger in the liver according to what you have skill for opening the wound, so that the two fingers can come out; then scrape the appendix that is outside the skin of the belly, as much as the white appendix does not appear white on all sides; then put your index finger in the direction of the liver, between the white appendix that is outside the skin of the belly and between the second appendix, and behind the belly, and between the second appendix; and move gently to the right side of the belly inside the skin of the belly, and hold the white appendix in your left hand high, and relieve the belly against the white appendix; and command the minister to extend the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the linen; and if you find anything, bring it out of the stomach; then take a needle or a thread made of twelve threads, and put it in the back part of the appendix, which is after the skin of the belly; then cover the threads that appear from the threads, as much as there are four threads; then assemble them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the appendix, which we have said is outside the skin of the belly, with a strong thread of two inches; then cover the threads with the thread, and form it into two inches, so that none of the vessels that are needed cannot enter the wound, that no pus gathers; and finally tie the thread according to the first thread, and after these two threads leave the appendix which is outside the skin of the belly, the length of one finger; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly has; then cover the part that is outside the skin of the belly, as we have said before; then apply moistened linen in oil, and put it on the wounds, and also apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have mentioned, after the incision, due to doubt of blood clotting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the wound remain until it stops bleeding; and if it takes too long to stop, then soak in hot vinegar, and apply what we have said, until it stops; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch that is together with the viscera, in a manner that you tie the veins, after the incision slightly above; then apply oil, and treat the abscess with what works, until the veins heal; and the treatment is as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes a tear or breakage in the same way as we have said, and it opens wide; and no one should cut into the intestines at this point, and if they do, it is little, and it should be repaired every hour; and if it remains too long at this point, then the wound or abscess believes that the intestine is cut; and this happens by the extension of the syphac that is at the tear, as we have said, because it is stretched, then it is softened and inflated the belly and opens; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and it is never cured in this way: and it is that the wounds are closed with a large needle between your hands, then cover the tear with the belly of the intestine enlarged according to the quantity of three fingers; and then remove the syphac that is outside the skin that covers it, then take the thread and put it on the belly of the syphac; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two bellies of the syphac above the head of the thread, and both; then remove the head of the thread, and do not cover the syphac or extend the flap or other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the sinews, remove the pus and heal the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The wound is contracted, and does not appear to be breaking, and the cauterization is quiet in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the boots is softened in some men, because the charcoal inside is softened, and it is easy to see; and when one wants to cure it, it is necessary to make the patient lie on their back, and cut the softened leather over the natural leather; then assemble the two pieces of leather at a seam, and if you see, cut the excess softened leather into three or four seams firmly; then sew between the seams, and treat the wound as with other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	forcibly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is not customary to speak of chastisement in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only in two ways: one is that the patient respond to chastisement when asked, and be treated with chastisement; and the other is because we often have to chastise some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rabbits and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastisement is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by pulling, we make our seat near the animal in high heat, until the sinews are softened and remain so; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	1. For the hip dislocation: it is necessary that you tame the beast, and press the skin of the thighs with your right hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and scrape each bone to the cop, when you have well burned them; and leave no trace of the sharp or subtle spicule that is on the bones; and this method of taming is better than that which is done by attraction, for the attraction may leave something of the thighs, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	1. Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite exists in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles open as wide as the natural shape of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes it secretes urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has a penis like a finger and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is that you cut off all the hairs stuck together, and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine sprays through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	For the tenting is a charred pole placed above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have also used it as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to apply the superfluity of the tenting to your hand or nails, and clean it lightly; and do not alter too much, as blood does not come out, then the cure of other cures until it is healed; and to another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and perhaps it will jump up, and it is according to the appearance of a snake, and for this they called the old «snake disease».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to cup, as we have said of the technique, and treat until it is healed.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratique is when the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or the uterus is small; and it is nature by birth, or accident by disease that has come to be; or it is due to a charm, or a subtle or sharp spice, and it is made in the marrow, or in the costal, or out of place, or whatever; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the look of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears nearby, then it is yours or the right one.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle swelling, and it is near the two lips, then quickly do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then press the two lips together firmly, until the subtle swelling is pressed out, and it is over the swelling; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the limb, and massage the woman every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and rough, then it is necessary to use a cupping vessel similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bone is broken, if it is bent and straightened; and have the medicines stanching blood, such as acacia, blood of dragon, incense, abundant amount of oil; then apply a large piece of dry plaster, so that the wound cannot stick together; and thus let it be long, and then apply a tent of dry linen; then treat other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a broken bone, if it is necessary to cover it this way, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually heal, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thrombosed ones, when they are in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, cannot be treated except by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the edge of the marsh, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then apply leeches and cut off the thrombus at its roots, then powder with restraining medicines such as acacia and sulfur and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet for an hour in cold water, then put her in a cold bath; if blood comes out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and scrape peels of green pomegranates and galls and similar things, and then take wheat flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he endures, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply suction cups to the back and breasts with force; then take the limb, and soak it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and apply heat to the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp, rough chief, if it needs covering as I have said of the thulium; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of boils from the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of boils come from the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and styes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chronic abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must mention in this treatment the chronic abscess that comes from the marsh, which is not one of the boils that coalesce; and if you know how to use iron, look at whether the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its appearance, and if it is accompanied by fever and heat, and if it turns red.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but let the pain subside; then place the injured part on a chair, and have two small stools where it can lean, and support it on its back, and bring its feet to the sides of the leg; and let its knees be spread, and put its arms away from its hips, and tie them tightly with a good bandage; then apply the splint to the right side of the chest, and maintain the instrument that opens the mouth of the wound, from which afterwards comes the shape; and when you see the instrument maintained, it is necessary to check the depth of the wound, so that what enters into the instrument does not go further than it should, and does not break the injured part; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument on top, and sterilize the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess is open and one makes it with their hand wide, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with spatula leeches; and when the wound is empty, put moistened tents in rose or green oil; and place the tent from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and place above the marsh and above the other clean moistened bandage in hot water or boiled herbs; then after two hours of poulticing, as long as it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound with a cloth of hot water and honey, and then with hot water or roots of lily and aristolochia are boiled; then reapply poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the marsh, it is necessary that you guard against cooking iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Midwifery is first in the bath that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs as you see the woman approaching, and desires to smell the armpit: then hasten the child to issue; then wash that child according to the natural figure, and is its own head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on his belly, so that the child issues soon; for as soon as he issues from his head, the second is with him, and is washed in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes above its feet, and comes forcefully to the chest or the neck, and the hands, or it comes over its belly, or sometimes, and is turned by chance upon its back, and by other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and subtle in these things, and if he errs and is deceived, I will show you all the figures as you should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out by natural issue, and the mother gives birth with great pain, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a seat, or the women hold her; and rub oil or fenugreek that has been cooked onto her back, and then give the bailiff a small spatula of this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And pierce the second joint, and cover it with a bandage until the moisture that is inside has been removed; and take the woman's belly so that the fetus descends, and if it does not, then you must clisterize the woman with a muskillaige of fenugrec with oil of seisament; then let her swallow it and vomit it out, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: then the fetus will now descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, then you must gently and gradually reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then lift the chair over the ground, and tie the woman, so that she does not fall during the lifting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cover the hands with a cloth that was previously placed at the crotch, and extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it is necessary to place it on its back; then turn it slowly and slowly, until it is level; then grasp both feet and extend them slowly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps just as it is born, command it to hold still, and extend its neck; if it does not, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it slowly and slowly, until it is in its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it is completely straight.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a handful of altee, and oil of sisament, and melted gum, and grind everything in the mortar; and put on the natural form of the woman inside and outside of this ointment, then make her sit in high temperature until above the ribs; and when she is softened, make her a mustard plaster, and put it on, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her spit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child over its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, one puts their hands gently and gently on its knees; then it should be laid on its back, and its feet hanging down, and lying on the bed; and gently folds its hands gently and gently, and then takes its hands on its stomach, and removes its clothing little by little until it is clean from below; and if the child does not cry, one takes its feet and forms them gently, then moves its stomach upwards, then one blows on its stomach; and slowly feeds the child a little and a little; and commands the woman to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out widely with a hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman and go; if she cannot go, place her on a bed, and straighten her legs; then relieve the muscle that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, sit her on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand; and hold the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command her to bear down until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother's
