I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient wash his hand, then turn it slowly and gently; when it is even, put on the natural oil of olive, as we have said, then command him to move it slowly; when you have done this, make him sit on a chair, and command him to grasp something; and make him spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, for all the other fingers.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this with all the other fingers, if the moisture is removed by gently pressing the finger against your nail and against its neck, and holding the face down, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then give the child inside, until you have put it in the right place, and command the woman to grasp something once: then it becomes loose.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often the case that twins are born, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if not named; I know that they are multiplied and are saved by the midwife who delivers them, who is tied to the bed; and sometimes they are born naturally as one at a time, just like we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born harshly, as we have said the care should be, and if the afterbirth is subtle, and she does what she should do quickly and lightly, and she does it in such a way that it is good for her health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, or seventh month, or more than fifteen months old, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise doctor, and it is necessary that the bale sage knows everything, because perhaps similar things happen to them; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When treating the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and if there is no result, and you are forced to handwork; it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be laid on her back, and her arms bent downwards, and her legs raised; and the assistant holds two fingers in the child's mouth, or she is tied to the bed if she is not treated by the removal of the child; then wipe the mouth of the child with mustard powder and fenugreek seed and linseed, then put the midwife's hands in these oils and powders; then gently feed the child with them, then give her a little warm water or milk that is suitable for her, and if the child is dressed with clothes that are not suitable for him, and if he has a fever, put the tube in his eyes or on his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or behind his beard or in his ears or on his ribs, and if he spits it out, put it in any of these places that we have said, until the thing is empty; and this is the form of the tube:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place it against another bone, or where you have skill, so that the extraction is even; and then set it evenly by moving one part and another, to make it move, and hold the bones together, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then use some of his two fingers' oil, and put it in that part, and pull the other part; and if it does not remain, then place this bone or higher up on the shoulder, and do this as much as it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you must wrap it up above the injury, until it is completely out; then cover it in the joint of the foot or at the knee, and so you must do in the other hand, and in both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the patient is a child and is large and has a sharp angle at the end, it is necessary to use a spatula with spinous processes between your fingers, and straighten the angle; or you can break it with an instrument called "almidach", of which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and in the same way, if the child has a great natural sharp angle; and then remove the bones with pliers, and if the patient's stomach is swollen and out of place, if it cannot be put back, cut it open; and if it is inflated in the abdomen or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the arrow is above its feet, it is a light attraction, and the wound to the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is sharp in the belly or in the groin, it is recommended that you extract it with a rolled-up cloth over your hand; and when the belly or groin is opened, as long as the wounds are clean; and if other members are also injured, and the patient remains conscious, then put your hand under their chin, and pull out the arrow from the mouth of the wound; then use one or two fingers, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the wound is retracted due to an abscess that has formed, do not force it, but manage moist and greasy things; and apply emollient poultices, and sieve in high mollifying and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the shoulder is dislocated above its socket, and you can put it back in place, follow what we have said about the living child; and if there is no way to do so, then treat it as you would with a fracture, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, follow what we have said about abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be stopped with high pressure, and then treat it with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted another about the other, and the other died also.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the buttocks, and they swelled so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and he thought for a long time, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive bandages, and some bones were stuck in them, and after some time others came out.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound and found many bones in it, until the woman was much better; and the woman thought for a long time like this, and there was a little blood on her skin; and I do not remember that chapter except that when the masters find an unusual thing, they know how to use help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	then comes the form of pressure, with which we open the books; and to II returns to II questions about II joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictive, and be made of smooth or boxwood; and the mouth of the fust should be two inches wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be two stoppers of this same wood, which are firmly fastened on both sides, half a palm or more in length; and these two stoppers are inserted into the mouth of the marsh when returning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, which appears more subtle and lighter, should be made of an even or boxwood rod, according to the appearance of needles; and it has two prongs, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the wound with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, the feet together and the legs spread, then drive the two prongs into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, as you would with needles, according to the amount that you want to open the mouth of the wound, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This tool is surrounded by many similar ones; and when the patient has them all prepared, the more they have, the faster the work, and higher the praise for their skill.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disregard the tool that you have not prepared, for their need is not excuseable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second joint is held in infancy, it is necessary to command the patient to hold their tongue, and then make them spit out the condition, and hold their hands at the mouth and nose; and if they vomit, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the pot, and make a syrup or covering, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a spoonful of syrup or covering in the mouth of the marsh, and the tongue until the vapors come into the mouth; then make them spit out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not much better, then command the patient to massage their right hand with olive oil or musk oil of altee, and then put it in its natural position, and find the second joint; and when they have found it, grasp it and stretch it gently and straight, so that the married does not prevent extraction; but move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and be dislocated.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the married's mouth is very tightly closed, we have said the cure of expectoration and fumigation of herbs; and if none of these things are possible, then guard that you do not force it; but it is better that what is at the mouth of the married, that you tie it to the neck of the woman, then syringe with tetrafarmaçon ointment; if it will take and return, and come out stronger; but nevertheless, when it does so, there comes a bad smell to the stomach and head, and increases the pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is therefore necessary to use incantations for the air, none of the ancients have experienced fumigation with cresses and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman during retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass similar to a cage, and one places the head subtly in its nature, and the others wide over the fire; and let the fumigations over the coals, and the tine until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet pierced the foundation, but it has been stupefied by some subtle swelling: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that swelling at its proper place, and not to pierce the space of the afterbirth, and to cover the wound so that she does not touch it; then place a moistened cloth with wine and oil on it, then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not set, put or insert a splint, and let it lie for some time, and it should be supported as the infant wants to go into the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never once comes this stench of pus or abscess; if it covers the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the deep fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodular and thicker than those that come above the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and becomes moist with white or subtle discharge, and never once are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosity when the pain makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the hip, and perforate the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you prick your finger or basement, and put a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you put a thin tent of lead, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no puncturing egestion or ventosity or ver, as we have said: cut so that it does not perforate more; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is located near the bladder or near a urinary duct, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be cured by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the joint of the hip, then the tendon is close to the bone; if there is no tortuosity and the pain is within, then it is stuck, and there is no cure by medicine or cauterization; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pain is hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then drive a spike, or a thick one if there is tortuosity, until you pierce the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your finger through the opening, feeling for the arrowhead; and if you sense between your fingers the shaft or the point, then remove it; if not, there is no need to struggle, as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is possible to heal some, but this rarely happens; and the aid that is given, if it is to heat the cauterizing iron according to the width of the fistula, as it was previously mentioned; and to push it all the way into the fistula, until it reaches beyond the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these charred pieces are removed, which are similar to a barbed arrowhead; then apply the healing of powdered burre, as long as those charred pieces are not released, then apply the cure of ointment, applying char and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If they are thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, nothing else can be healthy; and if it tries to escape between, and does not perforate just where it is based, and between the attempt and the tent a thick covering of char or syfac, and you see the fistula leading to the cure that follows the covering; if the cope of the beginning of the fistula, and before the tent, and then the cauterize after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and he will be delivered from the attempt, and closed; then wash those charged that seem like a quill of a goose, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot move it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: to know, the burning of these charred pieces, and the stopping of blood and the sealing of moisture; then cure the tents milled in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the wounds do not weep, and when the chars are burned in the wound; then cure the wound with hard char, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the foundation, and is away from the body, press on the top or foundation, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the cloth or the thread or the charcoal where it is about to pierce, unless there are other means of support and hope, by administering one of the three methods: whether you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut just above the foundation, or if you can put tents and cure as in the first; and do not leave too soon from the front, so that you do not cover the foundation that holds the base, and bring the excretions out through the opening; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and wipe it clean after it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or other appointed instrument; then clean the charred part of the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to hold back the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, it is where it costs at the base of the skin above the flesh, then take a probe pierced at the tip in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push the thread through and push the probe along the entire thread into the fistula until it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not found in the margin of the base inside, then push out the thread from that one, so that you push your other or base; and pull the top of the thread, and gather the two parts together, and hold them against each other, and let the thread rest for a while until the thread covers those that are between the two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then I will puncture it in all possible ways that you can, if it is not too far gone.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the bandage overly tight if it is too far gone, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiculated bony structure that is made into a fistula is very sharp and pointed on one side, and on the other part not, because we do not know what we should not touch, as you see here:
des emorroydes	des emorroydes
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes are in two ways: either they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood, and others have a little or a lot of pus, and some have a lot of pus, and some have a little or a lot of yellow or red pus, and some have a lot of pus, and the treatment for those inside the foundation is that you order the patient to sweat until they are dry in another room, as long as the foundation is not wet, and then you can tie them with needles, or hold them with your fingers, then cut them at their roots; and if the threads cannot be held by their moisture, take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; and pull them to both sides, then cut them, and powder over any hot powders that are in the cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, so treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, then cleanse the wound with a rough and sharp cleansing agent to remove what is inside the foundation, so that it can come out openly; and if the threads are thick, and the foundation is strong, the treatment is light; and it is that you pinch them with your fingers or needles, then cut them, and treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and do not fear the incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to stitch the wound in this way: take a thread of twisted wool, and pull it into a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and pierce the needle from the other side, and return the two ends of the thread outside the needle, and if it is wide; then tighten the thread properly, then loosen the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put above the wound a piece of linen cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it above the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; then let him rest until they heal, and when they are healed, then treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and firmly at the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occurs dryly and firmly at the base of the intestines, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset at the point of a sharp tool or your own nail, which does not allow moisture; then care for it as it should be until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, repeat the scraping stronger than before, until it is sound, and let it be scarred; then care for it until it is healed.
dou fremit	dryly trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice is a small appearance made on the chest, and it goes very far; and sometimes it finds the lungs, and one feels it like a shiver of cold, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose or a pen of vulture very strong, and place that quill over the shiver, until the circle around the shiver encircles it completely; then turn your hand to all the quill until you cover all around the shiver, and push it forward, and extract the shiver from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that the shiver is of a quill made of rain or iron in this form, and is thinly drawn out below and raised above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not mistake, to hold the first joint, and to press it; and if you see, then cauterize the heat, as it is before or in the chapter of the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one has ever made a cautery of silver or of iron, whether melted or in the form of a needle; and no one has ever made any of these small and large instruments, according to those which they are accustomed to use.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those which one should use in the treatment of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large cautery is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a dislocation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the wound is in one side II holes, and in the other I; and the belly is filled with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is perforated all around with small holes, and there is between each hole I inch of space, then sew together the edges with strong thread in X or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the wound is facing an instrument before a strong thread, then cicatrize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and oil or similar ointment applied to the head of the cast, then gently press it; then the attendant should apply the ministers to both hands together, until all the viscous parts are removed, then remove the cast, and relieve the pain in his legs at once, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cast him with the disease of uterine prolapse, and the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he recovers healthily, continue until he is completely healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	If they are embedded in the base or an abscess, then the poultice should be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin poultice above where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to how they are made, and according to the places or wounds that are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a spear, and cutting of sword or dagger, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that bleeds above the neck, or above the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, take care if it is an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and is large, and you doubt lightly of abscess: if you do this immediately clean the head itself if there is little blood from the wound, and clean the opposite part if necessary; and avoid the evils of overeating and heavy food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to clean, let him eat soft food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his bed; and put on the wound, if abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in stinging vinegar; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the wound has moved, put on some ointments, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a tailor's awl and similar, and the lips cannot come together due to tension, then sew them together, as I will say in wounds of the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be moved but only held by a small piece, then cover it with a hard char in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as testicles and cooked grain, like chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have to remove skin or flesh, and there is no bone, then cover the whole wound with charcoal, and pour in honey, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stanched by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have to remove it, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder that soothes as soon as the pain begins.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take a part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; fresh chalk three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly until it heals well and joins with all its own scabs; then tie it securely, and leave it undisturbed unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use chalk alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but only when the pain begins.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but use some ointments digested, or arrowroot flour made of honey and water, as long as it is not healed; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine needles; and I will tell you about the main fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and the main fractures, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other remedy than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, for it hurts bones and makes them recede; and do not put anything sharp over the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and the continuation of such things is with the brain, which is one of the highest members; but rather let the medicine be soft, like chalk washed in warm sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the cloth washed in warm sweet water, and other stones of this manner, and moist cloths.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with strips of cloth until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the hair is long and full of blood, pierce or go below the skin; if the artery is cut, and blood flows, stop it, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the veins, and the conductor is kept, by which the meat goes, if the horn goes over the canal of the neck, and do not touch the neck but put it back according to its natural shape; then gradually tighten, and leave it for some time, then cure dressings until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, take them all out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave them until the wound has healed and is aligned; and if the wound is fresh, powder over the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then follow the treatment as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or of dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a spear or dagger wound, and the wound is deep, look to see if there are hairs growing from the wound: cut them off as the pain is mortal; but if it is not deep, and it is fresh and full of blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood so that it does not harden immediately, and return to the heart, and cover the pain; but use attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and let it rest for three hours, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor will there be tremor of the heart from any other cause; and when you see good conditions, cut off the wound.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds and other treatments, until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed and worked, then there is a fistula; then treat as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword cut, and it is simple, or small, or at the back, then treat as one should in front; if it is large, then stitching; and if it is small, then powder, and if it has entered into bone, and has broken off pieces, then put them in the wound, and take out the foreign bodies if they are not decayed; and if they are not decayed, then leave the wound to heal, it will alleviate the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs is judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Belly rupture is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines escape, by which the insertion of them; and the suture is more painful, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one can put the intestines back in, if one does not put them back in exactly; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the heat, if they are put back in more carefully, and therefore the medium-sized wound is worse, because one must suture the intestines to their place as with other II And there are four ways of rupturing the belly: the two common sutures are in the belly suture, and the suture of other body wounds and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; and therefore they are more specific with the belly suture, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	When the wound is small, and nothing of the internal parts is injured, and it is a matter of putting back together, this is done in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the internal parts are inflamed from the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat the parts in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of dry herbs in cold water only, or cook them in boiling water with cipol and spike, and heat the internal parts until the inflammation is removed; and never do this without restraint, and it is necessary that one does not burn because of the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if the intestines are moist or high and misshapen, because by this they align quickly; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the instrument used to remove worms; and the first cure is to quiet the pain, for we should not cut without great necessity. And this is the instrument for cutting: it is cut from within the abdomen and from outside, and it forms the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, if you can put them back in their natural form in their own place, for this is best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part away from the belly, it is necessary to place the injured person on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part away from the belly, put the head and the foot higher than the other parts, and similarly, if the wound is in one of the two parts, make sure that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus manage as I have said for large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is at hand, then apply a remedy that covers the entire wound with one hand, and bring together the lips; this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you hold an needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound's width, leaving a space of about two fingers from the edge of the wound, and then pass a needle or a strong thread through the skin on both sides, as far as you can pierce that part, and bring together the two threads of the skin in four places; then tie the thread into a double knot around the needle from both sides, then evenly bring together the edges of the wound, leaving a space of about two fingers, and then pass another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you have done with the needles, until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be of medium thickness, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the whole skin, and thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason, they should be of medium thickness; and do not put the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so that they do not cut and open the wound before sewing; and then cover the edges of the needles so that they do not stick to the injured part at night, and put tents or cloths on the edges of the needles to hold them, and leave them until the wound is sewn; this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two to sew the second stitch, and it is that you bring together the edges of the skin and flesh in four places to an needle or a strong thread; and when you have pierced these edges all together, then remove the needle from the part where you started, as if you were sewing with a needle; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with fresh bandages after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in a place where none could be found; and I wiped the wound twice a day with old cotton and cleaned it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle and the thread from behind the cloth; when it has pierced through the right side, bring the head of the needle out on the wrong side where you have inserted the needle, and pierce it from the other side of the cloth from behind; and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave one part of the wound once, and then sew the other part, until the sewing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the main needles to the other main needle, in a similar manner: stick a needle or main needle close to the wounded part, and make it pierce only that one alone, and leave the two wounds; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part inside, the two wounds, and then pierce both from the front part inside, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If one says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, or one in each; and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who braid corsets; and so that when the tear is in the belly, it is sewn more painfully than other stitches of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you clean the fresh wound to all its blood, provided that the art has moved it, you must return to the intestine and the cost; then put the powder in a charcoal jar, and if the art has moved it, you must put any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and shave the hair, and be careful of the scissors, and the mirror; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, you must put cotton, as soon as it begins to close, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other medical knowledge in multiple situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, then it is necessary to treat lightly with oil of temperate heat, or with rose oil, and place it inside the wounds, and outside the bones; and if it causes pain or inflammation in the belly, and often happens, then you should counter with black wine clutches, and immediately if the inflammation comes to the intestine; and pierce inside, and cut out what is inside the large intestines, as they are easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is raw, and this is due to the presence of veins that are in it, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back in as you would the intestine when it is raw; and if it is old and turned black, then you must tie the part that is black, for there are veins and arteries in it; then cut away what is between the limbs, and hang the two ends from the part on the side of the wound outwards to align the extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, if it can be closed in some men, because I saw that one man was killed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and was prolapsed and became a fistula, and inside there was excrement and pus; I put care according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the openings were closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that the hairs were not in his intestines; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, they should be tied in such a way: take hot irons with large tongs, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the hot iron has opened the mouth, put it on top of the two lips, so that it holds its mouth open; and then cover the iron, and hold it in such a way that it cannot slip off, then put the other hot iron after in this manner until the wound is completely closed; and through the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the shoulder blade is burned internally and causes no harm to the joint, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the end of the intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thread with a thin silk thread, then pull the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back into the tear; and this way of stitching is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the hollow intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	that all wound or abscess, when it is covered, is generally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut and opened.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to the verity of the hard and white tissue, where there is no pain, and it is cut like the quill of an eagle; and sometimes it is clear and deep, and sometimes small and thick; sometimes small and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, except by one of the EIGHT causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard pus inside, and on the lips, which does not allow new pus to be formed; or there is too much pus; or the wounds are poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and flowed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas that is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to great veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the principal member, and similar ones.
