Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas that are of this kind are of great difficulty and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the joint that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to do it, take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, if the quill; and if the fistula is twisted, take a subtle tent of plaster, for the plasters penetrate around the twisting; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well encircle it with tents, clysterize one of the holes with medicine, for the moisture does not go from one hole to another, and cleanses; then carefully remove it, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is well covered in front, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press his hand, and the location where he feels it; and when you will know truly the location where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, cut according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the corrupted matter that is inside; and then cure as long as it is healthy, and if the fistula is deeply placed in the right place, it is necessary to cut as much as you can, then put soft tents in medicine, and push them into the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments with clean cloth, until they are healthy; and if it is not healthy by this, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves do not cause pain or harm to your principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove all the corruption until it is completely gone, then cure the things that were injured for as long as it takes until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, then do not go any further: if it is exposed and you wish to remove it as much as possible, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too late for the corruption, so there is no other remedy except to wait for nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tenailles, then straighten it with the appropriate tool, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, and do not leave any behind; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then heat and moisture and charcoal, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something stinking and putrefying to the wound, and leave it until the flesh is completely rotten around the bones, and then they will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, wait until the corruption has entirely rotted the bone, then reopen the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption remaining, and comes near to the bone; if it must be so, cover it all with the corruption, and cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and he was infected with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open; but the doctor by their folly opened it so high that the abscess was opened, and they poured in a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many more suffered from weakness and moisture of the body; and many doctors sought cure within two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was flowing through the wounds to great pain; and he became red the body of the young man, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming into contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore withdrew, and dug into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption was coming to the bone from inside; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and I thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with remedies, but I could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm of the bone, and treat it entirely, then I returned it with remedies; it was healed and healed quickly, and it did not require any further treatment except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood, it often happened, but he was completely cured, and in the place of the bone, a hard callus formed, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction throughout, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a piece of linen, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it not be extended upwards; and put another piece of linen larger than the first on top of the linen, and lay it on the callus above the bone, and extend the head, so that you remove the rotten callus outside, and uncover the callus above the place where you see it should be, so that it does not become rotten; and put a bandage or a poultice outside the bone to cover the rotten callus; and it should be done so that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotten and does not open, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, remove the filling from the whole tooth; then put the wax on one part to another part of the decay, and let the wax be as long as possible from the decay, as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, cut the joint where the decay is, and let the bone or what it contains from the other part; and if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way than to cover it; and if the decay is at the tip of the hand or foot, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you should inquire about this decay, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not make the vein or nerve opposite; and know that the tools for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you should arrange each tool according to the likeness of the work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have to use according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	with great heat
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints will rot either due to their own condition or due to weakness; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicines, and it does not improve, then you must cut off that member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes by death or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards becomes darker, then those corrosions spread from member to member, and take hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cut off, and if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give them any time to come to your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the copper is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the copper at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do as follows when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, if the copper after the other joint; and if it comes to the bone, if the copper all the bone; and if it goes up the leg, if the copper at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than the patient's death; and the manner of the copper or the bandage for the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend some bandages on one side, and some bandages on the other side, and uncover the bone until it is exposed; then the copper or bandage, and put a piece of linen on each part so that the copper does not touch the healthy flesh, and comes to the injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows when you are working, cauterize the limb immediately with strong fire, or apply some powders that stop the bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a clean bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man who was in great pain: a black spot appeared on his skin that seemed like burning fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his chest, spreading all over his body; and when the honorable ones saw the corrosion, they covered the wound, and he was healed; but long after that, the corrosion appeared on his arm, and it came to me, and I put things on his wound after cleaning the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his home, and covered his wound, and was healed; and I have not told you anything else except for what is done in other cases.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a lean limb, and it lingers so long that it causes a great collection of pus; then it bursts and perforates, and the pus escapes, as if from a vessel; and the skin above is also as delicate as cloth, and does not corrode the bone, nor the nerve, and such a disease is called "sinus", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the outside, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cover that skin all around, and specifically when it is delicate, as if it were cloth; and it does not corrode for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is hardened and the corruption is not yet formed in the bone, and the skin is charred, then use this ointment: look if the breasts are large, and the nipples smell badly, then make an Egyptian medicine as follows: take equal parts of milk, oil, and lentils, cook them in a pot over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then add water according to your need, and make it into a thick or thin paste, and apply it to the breasts, and bind it tightly; let the ointment remain on for two hours, then remove it by wiping; do this many times until the breasts are clean and soft; if the pain is too great, and the Egyptian medicine and the ash water do not help, then use a thin paste of honey and wine, where the honey has the property to cleanse and the wine makes the skin soft; and when you have done this, and you have confirmed that the breasts are clean, then apply a definite plaster made with rose oil and wine, or use some medicines and ointments, as I have mentioned their properties for treating wounds; and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the ointment cannot enter, then enlarge it with a small needle, and put in an Egyptian tent or basilicon ointment until it is wide enough; and if the wound is too large, then let it remain open for as long as the ointment can enter, and if the nipple that is above the ointment is also affected, then cover it with a cloth or the lower part of the bandage where the ointment is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bone is broken, do not leave any charcoal on it; and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bone moves to the lowest point where it is, for when the bone is broken, do not leave any charcoal on it, and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way: that the bone moves lightly downwards, and leaves nothing of the bone; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and place it on the cloth that covers all the wound; then cover the forces at the point of the bone a little more than the first, since they are firmly attached to the other cloth according to the quantity of the bone, and place it on the bone to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the bone, often remove to align the bone, and see what comes from the bone, whether it is poison or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take precaution if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in a certain way and you see the nature that springs up over the cloth, then remove the bandage and approach health; and then remove it in the morning, or the next day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is ingested undigested after many days, break it up so that the breast does not turn bad.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take long time to heal their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food is ingested after many days, break it up so that the breast does not turn bad; and if the breast takes a long time to harden, and is far away, use medicines of moist substance and dry in virtue, such as oil of roses, and the last medicine is vitriol, and it is the best medicine; take oil of roses, and mix with old wine evenly in substance; then cook and use; and the same thing is made good when boiled and grown, when oil of roses is not present, or you take wormwood and aloe and incense, and grind it, and the powder on the honey as it is on the fire; and then apply the cloth, and place it on the breast, and never administer a physician long, and roots of lily celestial, which is also like flour and hundred; and use simple or compound: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use; and if the cure is long and not cured by this cure, then break up the corruption and make impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs; if the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elbow
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the elbow due to a pouch of the hand, or a pocket, or by chance it arises in other places; and when it is opened, and no care is taken, if the abscess spreads, and corrodes and drips blood so much that it reaches the root of the elbow, and perhaps corrodes all of it; and there comes corrosions just to the bone, until it causes a strong stench, and the affected part is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not improve, then you must remove all the excess that remains of the elbow, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are very helpful when the bones are healthy and the joint is healthy; and if the joint is close to the skin and begins to poke, and the wound, then it is necessary to remove the iron from the joint that does not pierce the skin, and place it above, and gently and lightly cover this joint with medicines of burning and corrosive nature to eliminate everything; then cure the pain until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it and remove it, because as much as the bone rots and is, it cannot be healed; and if you see the other rotting, then cover it with a bandage as mentioned above, then cure it until it is healthy; and if it is fierce, and bleeding, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary to first cleanse it; then cover the joint with a thin, sharp cut across, and make sure that the cut does not reach the skin that is outside the joint, because the pains would be too great; and if there is, then place something above that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of a sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The blisters that arise in the hands of some men are all charred, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have splinters, and sometimes they have thorns, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or in any other way.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who arise in no other way of the joint do not move, and those who arise at the joint of the joint may move; the size of the charred one is light, in the manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who arise at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you have the copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be placed at the back, it is necessary that you first cut the round bone to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then cure it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The similar things that come together come from birth, or from the wounding of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the wounding, so that the one that must return according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of thin leather, until the wounds are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to either of its two ends with the palm, then adjust it as it should be.
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large and swollen with excessive melancholy, which come from many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you must administer no purgative of clay, and then the healthy bishop's herb.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of the iron is in two ways: one is to adjust it and remove the black blood; and the other way is to open the vein and remove all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this way: first, the first leg of the sharp hot water very strongly, until the large without subtiliez, then strain the leg with the bad side below the hip; then cut the vein in the groin, or in II or III, of a wide incision, then release and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, as much as much of such can suffer the virtues of the bad side; and then tie it, and command that he be shaved with meat broth; and repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and not to the bad side.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the shoulder according to this method: if there is much hair, first shave the leg with the bad joint, then put it in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins; if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then apply a cloth soaked in warm water to the long vein at the back of the knee, or in the part below the knee; then rub the skin at every part until it appears when touched; it will appear red and black, and look like a white rope; then draw out the blood from the vein, as much as it takes to make the skin appear, and then let it rest for three days; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then apply it to the wound, as you have done before; then apply another bandage to the other side, if you have experience in such matters; then let it rest, and apply a poultice to the second bandage; then cut the bandage from one end to the other, until it is all gone, then apply; and if you cannot draw and lift it, insert an awl through the thread strongly doubled, and pull and draw it, and draw out the blood from the thread, turning your hand from one side to the other, as much as there is; be careful that it does not stick, for if it sticks, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it causes harm to the joint; and when you have treated it all, put a soft cloth moistened with wine and rose oil on the wound of the sore place; and cure until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the limb is bent and twisted and swollen all together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must torment it but do not cover it, and treat it as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron that covers the limb if it is hooked and does not cut through, so it does not cover the vein; and it is large in size, because if it were fine, it would cover the vein, but if it is large as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inflamed in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises from another part than the legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the flesh and blood, inflamed between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are such that it comes in the leg a very large inflammation, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound is open, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of plaster the size of one and a half palm's breadth by two palms in width, and the nose, and leave the plaster on the leg, and every time it is not there, if it wraps around the plaster, and the nose; and if it is too long, then take part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it will retreat into the flesh, and cause abscess and putrefaction in the limb, and severe illness; therefore it is necessary that it be treated very little by little near the top, and nothing remains or rots; and this wound never occurs when it is treated from the palms of length, or ten, and some have come to me, to which it issued ten palms in length, and when you cover it, if it bursts or punctures, and pierces deep, so that everything comes out; and let the matter inside be removed, and administer medicines by injection for putrefaction every day, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never rain on this vein, and especially when it opens into the joint of the thumb, or the little finger, and it often causes much pain, and from which it suddenly falls; therefore, as we have said before, cure it accordingly.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	births between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down the body, and is felt by all members in succession, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, such as worms and lumbricus and ascarides or intestinal worms; and there is doubt about its harm, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the brain, perhaps it enters, and destroys the brain; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that it needs to be cured and drawn, then you can only do so when it goes: therefore it is necessary to hold the limb above and away from a very tightly bound bandage, then cut through it and draw it out, and if it comes out in front of the char, and you do not pull it out, then cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, then hold it away from it well, then cut through it and draw it out; and it is necessary to use the bandage of healing for the bodies of medicines soluble for the humors which cause diseases, and if it becomes putrid, then use it for cooking.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and then moves from one limb to another; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a woman with pain, and she revealed one of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of that arm; and soon after, I saw it rise as if a snake were at the shoulder, more quickly than anything, just like live silver when it cuts through flesh to another; the pain departed from that limb, and went into the shoulder, and then a little later it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she had turned around inside her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease move in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen that it was possible for one member to move to another, but I had not seen it in this way; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and because that constraint appeared; and it did not appear in this way to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it opens up as we have described, then hold it above and below firmly, and then cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the cause of the constraint, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the types of bodies they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and blunted ones; and those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with pieces; and one that pierces any member, depending on the manner: if it pierces in a principal member, like the neck, head, heart, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: then you must proceed with the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various conditions; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and perforates the bone, and the face that is above the head, is when there is blindness and dizziness and vertigo and fainting, and inflammation and fainting of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps it is the speech and voice; and the white discharge from the wound, resembling pus, and also like boiling water, and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the shoulder when it dislocates or breaks, are that it is near the right breast, and also feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not empty; and perhaps the shoulder moves like the chicken, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore without doubt the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow does not enter the body is that without any bubbles coming out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and it breathes high and seeks the warmth.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow dislocates in the skin, it is below the small ribs; and it throws out great blood and great pain and breaths; and they move all the member of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead or stomach, by chance, falls out of the wound, nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead or stomach falls out of the wound without any intestines protruding, there is no hope for the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows out, and the pain is very great: cut open the wound as it is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and back and spine and hips and knees, and the member similar, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man who was shot in the calf at the root of the knee: I tried to remove it, and pulled it out from the other side, away from the ear grease, and he was healed quickly without much pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And pulled out an arrow that had been shot into the oil grease away from the paper away from the skin, and the arrow was intact, only reaching the tip of the wound, and it was a large arrow like a Turkish spear, made of all light iron without ears; the wound was healed, and nothing bad happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I removed an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I cut off the barbs, and carefully worked until I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I removed an arrow from a man, who had it in his neck or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and widened it, and carefully removed it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you want to remove an arrow from a man who had it in his back or shoulder, and the wound was healed over; and the arrow remained inside, and his natural conditions did not change, and he found no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man, who had an arrow in his face, and was laid on the wound; and thus remained without suffering great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was removed from the man of the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely removed, I was called to the care after it had been out for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a very fine needle, and felt nothing; and he felt pain and pricking from his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow that I put on the wound with a strong digestive agent, because the wounds did not swell; and it appeared to me that the arrows were coming out.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the ointment later, and immediately healed the wound, and the pain lasted a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put medicine with a corrosive agent on the wound later, as long as it was open, and I tried to remove it, and felt the tip of the arrow inside; then I inserted more of that corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound, until the patient clearly showed me where the arrow was; and it passed well through the wound in about four months, and then it discharged the splinters, and one part and another, and could not be removed; therefore I continued to subtly and ingeniously manipulate instruments, until I got the arrow well made, according to how its form would come out at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nonetheless, and it was sewn up, and the injuries were healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you might place your care on what I did not say, for books cannot comprehend everything; but wise masters understand many things, and know what is present and lacking, thus they find new work and new tools for the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the body unless in two ways: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and the one that exits by the way it entered is an arrow through the muscles, and has never exited once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her wait until the charred flesh is completely surrounded and softened; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot get out, let her wait for several days, and move it every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, then pierce all around with a subtle needle, until the flesh around is expanded, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly's ventricles, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned above to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but let it wait until it is even after several days, because if the arrow comes towards the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not come out by itself, and remains there for several days without causing harm, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is deeply stuck and cannot be pulled out, then apply tar as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body and cannot be seen, then seek a skilled surgeon to remove it; and if you feel it, then use any suitable instrument to remove it; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then leave it until the wound is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow that hold it in place, then carefully cut off the part that is stuck deeply, and then break or crush the ears of the arrow until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow while removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, then pull the limb towards the body until it is fully extended, then pull it back, for the extraction must be done gently.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the bleeding from the vein goes against you, then follow the advice we have given in our chapter on treatment; and guard against incising the nerve and the vein, and use caution as you draw out the arrow without causing harm, quickly or slowly, tightly or loosely; and put the wound back according to its original form when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do it, then put it back according to what the signs tell you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place where one can see or feel it: cut then above, as far as the barbs can be taken, and then extract it: if it has now broken.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out; and if there is any of the arrow left, and you see that it has pierced everything, and if it is sharp, and you administer it gently, so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrow is caught, pull the instrument in with the point entering, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you cut out the entire piece where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces or sticks in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is near, and you can cut it off, then cover the wound if possible; do not cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, then treat the wound as appropriate, and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is like an owl's beak, and this is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the beak of a bird, to stick at the point of the arrow, as in this way:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs for sticking and for holding is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that can be tapped from, of which there are 16 main ones, namely: two that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples, and the two veins that are in the armpits of the shoulders, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two jugular veins that are on the neck; and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly bled from are three in each arm: one is the cervical, and is on the left side, and is called by the common people "the neck vein"; and the middle one is called "the breast vein", and is composed of the cervical and the basilic, and is called by the common people "the chest vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and is called by the common people "the stomach vein", and is above the fossa, and is that which is bled from, which opens manifestly into the hollow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the auricular and the annular, and it is on the right arm; and in the leg and hand there are three veins: one is outside the corbeure of the left costeit chest, and the second one is at the ankle of the right costeit; and the third one which is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other costei; and in the other leg there are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The first sentence is: "For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The treatment of the two arteries that are in the two temples is to puncture them with a needle, and then insert a seton, and plug them with custom-made wool; and the quality of this treatment is as I said: it is that the pain is strange, so much so that the two veins appear openly; and it feels like the hair is detached from the side of your head, then sign of inflammation; then lift the skin above the vein at the top of your forehead, and pull out the needle, and lift the vein upwards, and cover it, as you did in the other two veins, and treat the blood according to your necessity; then remove the pain, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this and its treatment and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the health of the cephalic diseases of the face, and headaches, and dizziness; and the quality of the disease is such that the pain strains his neck, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healthy and never again in a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	It is not necessary that the flames be too hot; and the safe way is to hold it away from the bone, for fear of breaking the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The safe way to treat the two veins that are in the two armpits is to hold it at the elbow, and at the root, and at the shoulder, and at the back of the neck, and at diseases of the face; and the quality of their treatment is that the pain is strained by twisting any part, as before; then the safe way, and let the treatment be done from a little distance away from the flame, a little long and wide, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, by chance it may break; then apply pressure to the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie with a thread, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vinegar of the vein is good for a headache, and for swelling, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and constantly when it is ancient; and the quality of the vinegar is that the pains strain their neck, then strain their vein to your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space that is between the II nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will begin to stop now; and do not move too much in the beginning, and apply pressure to the blood according to your need, then tie it for one night, because it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
