Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two ingredients helps to narrow the alainne, and at the beginning of the melting, and with many diseases, and with impetigo, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is such that the pains strange their col out of one and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pain, and the pains sit on the first seat, then clean the wound long a little widely, then drain the blood frequently, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other side in the other wound, then remove the ligature, and hold the wounds steadily, that the pains do not strangle; and let it be applied just before morning, that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the liver above helps in the mouth, and prevents corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and pain and swelling inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of this health is to make the pain disappear in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that there are small black veins around them: match both, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, match the largest of each part, and do the same for both veins that are above and below, because it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's swelling
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The swelling of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the swelling of the cephalic, and it is from the tightness of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the swelling is that the diseases lie between your hands before the sun, and you lift up the tongue, and look outside on each side a black vein: heal both, and do not move too much, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pinching at all the flame mirroring large, or by a delicate way if they cut through, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and delicate according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very famous, and it is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has a job to open the veins that are closed by large blood clots, and contain large blood and disturbance; and this is the form of the flame mirror.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicately pointed, and is for cleaning the thin veins, where there is thin blood clot.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the shoulder, and where the stomach; and it is important for the cleaner to clean well, and to remove the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then it should be staunched, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with fire, but cut off as we have done with anus.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must reset it and change it; or you want to remove any rain from it, or you save in its place the vein of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut off with fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see that the vein of the arm is known, then it is also necessary to reset the arm until you touch the vein; then sign the vein of the wrist, and then bind the arm, and cut off the vein with fire as we have said; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it emerge high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, it is from an artery: then hurry, and put your hand long on it, then remove your hand when the blood stops flowing, which often happens; hold the arm still, and let it be, and do not move the hairs; and bear the pain, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood does not stop flowing, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the main vein will retract; and the blood stops flowing.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a sharp needle from a hypodermic syringe, and make it into a hook, and take one of the halves and tie it securely to the other end; if it is not stained, that is good; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping of the blood does not last for many positions of the small wound, and the position of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The cleansing of the vein in the middle helps that it treats blood above and below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the cleaner to search for the vein that is below, and if it does not appear immediately, and he finds the vein, he inflates it and the wound heals, and perhaps it cannot be healed; and this vein opens often, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must use the cleaning instrument again; and exclude the vein from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The puncturing of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes; and it is best to puncture at the olive oil or mint flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because it has no nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is best to seek the lightest vein, and do not harm anything if you must the first time, and restart; and by chance, some men's veins swell at first, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about healing is that healing is only done to maintain health and to prevent diseases from coming; and healing should be done in one of the three veins that are: cephalic, basilic, and median; and if you should heal at the beginning of the day, and in autumn and winter after fasting, when the sign of repletion appears; and if you should heal on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing that is administered to diseases has no determined time, but rather it depends on the urgency of the hour or the need; and it should not be healed in children under 14 years old, nor pregnant women except for four months until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not allow those who have passed sixty years to undergo surgery.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If anyone wishes to undergo surgery, it is necessary for him to cleanse his intestines with a light clyster if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful superfluities into the principal members; and one should not undergo surgery if he is too fat from meats, or if he is bloated, or if he has hydros; and if one wishes to undergo surgery after colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent traveling, pregnancy, nursing, and all the virtues of the arm or body; then subtly draw out the humors, as much as possible without being too thin, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then take a bath or do nothing that might hinder drawing out the blood, to thin the blood, and to heal from the vein during the third hour, as we have said; and guard against work, needlework, luxury, and similar things; and be tied and joined, and let the surgeon be higher than those who are being operated on, and let him rub his hand twice or three times, then gently move the limb above the middle, for when it is too stiff or weak, it cannot correct itself; and then rub the wound with the palm of his hand until the veins swell, and feel if they bleed; then moisten the wound with a drop of old oil, then place his right hand on top of the vein of the wound where he wishes to operate, so that the vein does not fail to be drawn.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the scribe, and some that are plain in their thinness, such that when one puts them over the flame, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if the scribe opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary for the scribe to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the scribe opens the vein the first time, it is good; but if not, then he should restart a little below that place or above hastily, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the joint is swollen, and the pain subsides, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will form; do not enter water, then begin cleaning again if it suits him; and if the wound is small, or the skin is slightly cut and you doubt that there is as much blood as you saw, then apply the fire directly to the wound; and work carefully, as long as the joint is swollen; for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And if you see the joint swollen, do not begin cleaning again, and put a little oil on it, for it reduces the flow of blood, and is soothing in this joint like oil; and thus administer the oil in every cleaning to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing is done with triangular and bandage dressings, when they are placed on the wound; and gently remove the skin when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there are large abscesses that often occur, even when it is not healed until this time or the opening of the vein is small, then you must hurry, and place an absorbent sponge soaked in boiling and salted water on the limb for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any time without turning black or green, then you must not remove it; and if you see, place something of aloes or of myrrh mixed in honey or jelly on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the pus on the base of the cathedral: put your hand over it, and if you compress the limb too much with your hand, that is the wrong appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything on it that we have said, for by chance you might cut the artery; but make a dry bandage to strengthen the limb, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it large, let it bleed until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is wounded and has a profession of arrow extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for the weak, do the opposite, and let them rest often, and they should be bandaged by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of bandaging is safe from the corrosion of arrows and the compression of nerves, and it is better than the bandaging done long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one who has a tendency towards the bandaging, it is appropriate to give bread soaked in the juice of grated apples; if they are hot-blooded, take out the arrow three or four times; and if they are cold-blooded, change the bread soaked in honey syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pales at the sight of blood after losing much blood, then it is necessary for him to drink a broth of meat and an aromatic syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to stretch out his arm and bleed again, then it is necessary when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleeds a little bit at a time, according to the amount of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bleed his arm again after the first bleeding, and he is very weak, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And those who wish to heal on the other side, they must heal at the second hour or at night.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood inside the body that is already heated, and causes fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it ceases to bleed; then one must wait for all the conditions of healing, and put one's hand on the pulses when they are healed, so that the dead does not return in place of the pulse, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent; and it does not matter if you see the arm becoming weak, and making blood come out the second time, and the vein is closed, that one presses firmly; or if it is crooked, one stretches the arm quickly, for this would be bad; but let it heal the second time; or if the bleeding does not stop at the point of the flame, and put a small amount of salt re-dissolved in boiling water, and press firmly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If it is seen that it is swollen, let it alone and do not press it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood the second time, let it be drawn from the same limb or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is drawn in place of the arm because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of drawing blood is that the hairs are inserted in hot water until they become red; then it is moved gently so that the vein appears well, then draw blood through the middle, not too narrow or too long; and let the punctures be wide, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be released, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out until you have enough; and if it is still stuck, do not turn the hand in hot water again, for it causes more harm than good; and drawing blood from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the blood flows out; if the salve is against the grain, and if you apply it with the whole hand, it will not hurt; and do not change it too quickly, for the nerves are all exposed to the char, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, put oil and silk on the wound to stitch quickly, and do this for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The right hand sinew of the forearm is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sinew of the saphenous vein is good for all diseases that are outside the body, such as marsh diseases, and retention of fluids, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and legs in old age, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sinew is that the diseases are driven out quickly in hot water, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and tied above the joint; and the vein is at the elbow, and by passing through the elbow much rain goes out; therefore the sinew of the large vein, or at the elbow, is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have the healthy ones above the wound, and you guard against the nerves that are exposed, and the healthy one crosses as in covering; and let the flames be behind.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out without harm, put the wound in the high place, and let the blood drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if it must be bandaged the first time, start the second one above a little, because the legs are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the bandage of the other wound equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the wound is at the knee of the thigh, and its bandage is worth the pain of the back, when it is for an arrow.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his sanity are such that the hairs between or in bathing, and is strange above the knee four times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and across; and it is better to cover it, for the legs are clean, and it is very often done by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not heal it, then no rain of those who open or close two pints, and towards the small toe, and guard against the nerves; and correct so much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put above cotton and hold it steady; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either at all times, or not at all; and suction that is done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is entirely on the back; and the others are under the collarbone; and the other two are on the ribs; and the suction below the chin; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the knees; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction on the heels; and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with the drawing of blood; and it should not be administered, neither at all times nor not at all, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessary for diseases, one must venesect, or by habit, if we mistrust the patient, let us venesect every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each ten; for there are some who, when they have business to venesect, have great pain; and some who experience repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who taste blood in their mouth, and swallow it, and reach for blood; and there are some who sing, and see through a bloody mist and drown and die and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The cleansing of the muscle helps to alleviate the headache… that comes from them, and it should only be done after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in place of the cleansing of the cephalic, and it should only be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because this does great harm; and for this reason, it should not be used by those who are guards or who have other cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often become unconscious, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little lower due to the uncertainty of unconsciousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse on the neck is in place of the head and the chin, and therefore it is necessary to place it at the narrowest point, and at the front of the throat, and everywhere, and for replenishment; and it should be placed a little loosely, because if it is held too tightly, it causes unconsciousness or stomach pain and pain in the chest.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventouse on the two ribs of the neck is necessary for head pain, and itching and numbness, and choking, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the health of the chin; and it is necessary to command the patient to place his hand when putting it on, so that he does not compress the artery, and does not cause bleeding from the blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The winds of the mouth cause disease in the mouth, and decay of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the shoulders cause disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The winds of the elbows cause as much harm as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and commands the physician that he does not prick too much in front, for the bones are bare of flesh, and can be damaged by nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should be used for diseases of the foundation, and for maladies of dislocation, and it must be a large and made of metal, which can draw well; and by chance, if it is too thin, it will break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are used openly, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are useful for old pains of rheumatism, and marsh fever, and of the bladder, and remove swelling; and they are in the place of the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and cause pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is that you first apply it empty and quickly fill it, then press it firmly and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the affected area become red and swollen, and the blood clots appear; then, remove the cups, and take care of the body's condition, for there are those who have tender skin and clear pores: if necessary, strike once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the blood clots.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the joint is still very painful, you should strike it a third time; and when we want to pull out the arrow slowly and gradually, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw out a lot of blood, we should often repeat it; and if the joint is still painful, we should strike it in front, and let the cut be made deeply, which is suitable for those who have thick skin and are strong, and who have sharp points, that you apply the oils of an appetite-stimulating and dissolving: if it is in summer, of violet oil or sweet almond oil or squash seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal, lily, camomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amber, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who has to stretch a wide and large wound, should not put any oil, but it should be washed after the ventilation of hot rosewater, or cold rosewater, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from asafetida, or rosewater, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superfluities rise from old wine, or from vinegar of sour, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be washed with a suction device before the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and they should not sleep immediately after the enema, and it is good that they move around, when they should be enemaed and when they are enemaed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are sick with colic and without are too full and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce at the sauce, and similar things; and mild foods, and mustard of Chastel, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution should take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little juice, and little pinches of peppercorns and peacocks; and the day they want to vomit, they should drink more than they eat; and it is necessary to give some men once in a while a triangular or muscat before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main members; and it is subtle for the sick, but only those who are chaste should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the skin are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the gout, and on the stomach and the belly and the ribs and the hip, for these members do not suffer from being pierced with needles, except to draw blood from one member to another, as we put suction cups on the breasts when the baby is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and on the belly to soften the member; and to remove pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, if by its attractive power it happens to remove the abscess, or to dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for their sweetness alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with hot, watery vapor, as in diseases of the chest, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot, boiling water, or with hot water in which herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two wide and half-palm-sized openings at the front, and has or costitutives around the middle one small hole, as to put a needle, and it is of brass, sulfur before so that it does not burn the hair when putting it on the limb; and it has in the middle a thin rod of brass or iron, to put a candle, and they are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suctions of children are different from those of old people, and thin people are different from fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction device on the member: take the candle of wax or the linen cloth, and put it inside the suction device through the rod that is inside the suction device, so that the flame may not burn the hairs; then put it on the member, and one must do so above the blistered spots that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to remove it, one can remove the suction device; and take the linen cloth as before, and restart often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction device that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there is no rod or blister; and it is not administered until it is completely flat, and it is placed on the member alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not indicated for use except in members where one cannot place bandages due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, such as ears or nose, and others; and the quality of using sansues is that when you remove sansues that are in high places, such as the eyes, and similar things, take them; and put them in a high place, as long as they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies; and then wash them with blood and bandages, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are flat and dry, if it is a part where one can place bandages, place them, for this is very good afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb from the elbow, and then from the shoulder, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the course of the sinews, then wipe the linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the sinew is cleansed; and if the sinew multiplies, then put vitriol shattered glass, or salve, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you put half of pounded beans on the wound, and leave them until they burn the limb, it will stop now; and if you have more, then take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the snakes will not take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you stick a needle so that the snake bites it, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will swell; and when you see that they are about to burst, powder them with a little aloe and ground salt, or with ashes, they will now be ready.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear child, that the foolish man thinks that this chapter has never been seen in any of the old books, nor have they ever read any letter about it; and for this reason the science is unknown in our land, because I have never found any good one; and I do not know anything, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that will be used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say or prologue of this book the summary of the language and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or wound comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to clean the wound on both sides, if nothing happens, as weakness of the body, or children, or elders; or if the joint is not very loose, or too stiff; and use sharp remedies, that is to say, sharp remedies, and eye ointment and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and do not use any heavy meats, and do not fill up too much with food that fills the veins of blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess, or spreading of matter to the member; then the wounds return to their previous government as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one massage the painful joints that are large and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in boiling water, and ribs, and tests, and pies, and chicken, and eggs, and fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the massage, one should avoid making movements that cause pain and the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And be aware that the broken bones of old people and the decrepit cannot be properly healed or joined according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, neither those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but instead, one should reset the broken bone above the joint and hold the member together, as it was before; and do not let it rest completely, and for this reason, it is necessary to massage with large pieces of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go through the bone, and others in soaking, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture through a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind there is its own method, and its proper tool in the restoration, according to what the memory brings to its mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the bone is twisted, and open well by deficiency, and it is to the pressing of the hand; and when there is no tortuosity or it is not to the touch, and the pains are not much, if there is no fracture; but it can still have tortuosity, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in the armpit, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them back together evenly, as if incising an abscess; and if it is hard and comes, do not let any joint remain, until the abscess is calm; then gently and safely place it on the muscle that you can easily and safely move, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of that where he has pieces, then restrain it as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	If the bone is broken into pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two cords, or to one cord and at your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member broken are separated, if you can, join them in their proper places with the help that you can, and guard that by your work no harmful injury or pain comes; and well set the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if the bone feels not quite right in your hand: if it is well bent, and you do not hold it too tightly, and do not press it as those who bring by their work abscess and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is injured, if you properly restrain the painful part so it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and make sure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet healed, and you should put it in a position that it feels no pain; and make sure it is properly aligned, so that deformity does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the member broken are different in size and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with soft linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as the thighs: cover them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it equally in all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap it around lightly, three or four times according to the size of the member, and hold your hand a little on each side, then go above the fracture and hold it less, than the fracture gradually move away from the fracture; then soften the bandage little by little, until you feel a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage, and return around the other side of the broken bone; then go to the part away from the fracture, and hold it gently, neither too hard nor too firmly, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the bandages linen or cloth strips, until they are all even, then tie everything above with a bend, and then put your well-made shoes on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, put a soothing ointment on it, and what opens the abscess, and leave it in place for some time; then apply pressure with something sterile, such as half of a wide blade cut cleanly, or wooden splints, or palm leaves, and they should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the sterile strip that one puts over the wound should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the limb, whether small or large; then apply pressure with the strips as you did in the first layer, then tie them up evenly, as in the first layer over the break; the tighter the better, but not too much; and it is best if the strings are of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be made of linen; for if the strings are too thick, as I have seen in some works of the folk who make their own bindings with twisted linen threads, and this is great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is best that there be at least one finger's breadth between each strip.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the hairs are pricked by the thorns after straightening them in their proper place, then put some unwoven linen or straw between them so they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a splint and the bandages are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs at once on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the limbs are large, one should not put splints on them until after five or seven days, or more according to your safety from abscess; and get the way of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and twist: and take some flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, and mix it with much egg, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it is the common way of the plaster restoring fracture to many positions, and especially to women and small children, because it is not too hard or too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making plaster to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take alabaster and lavender and enule and asafetida and Arabic gum and mugwort, each 1 part; myrrh and aloes, each 5 parts; alechil 8 parts; and grind them into a powder, and mix with honey; if the humor of the body is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it heals broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of making plaster that is good for twists: take mugwort and valerian, each 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, each 8 parts; bolic armenic 10 parts; grind them well and mix with honey or a lot of honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of treating joints and bones that have been dislocated from their sockets, and to relieve the pain, and to use the bone and the fracture: take a new leaf, and grind it in oil and cooked oil, and put it on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not last long, but it is good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of treating broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth partridge leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of treating the fracture of a bone and to alleviate the remaining pain from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are cold, mix with moist or dry coriander powder, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying more than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of wormwood, linseed, balm, mint, and savory, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from all one part; and grind, and mix with salt powder, or sweet powder, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put above a broken limb for restoring it but rather use a poultice made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put above a broken limb for restoring it, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to apply a poultice that is good for the wound and pain: take mallows and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and viscum, and seal equally, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, release it a little later, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, or if they do not move the bones of their joint; then do not release it by force again. If pain comes to the limb, or pruritus, without rest or inflammation, quickly release it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light bandage, and moisten with sea water, and pour in hot, and raise the limb, until the pruritus ceases, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with hot or rose oil, and tie up with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then start the subtle bandage again, and a little bit of plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plastering and of bandaging, if it restarts, as you did previously evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, then do not remove it for three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it twenty days, as long as the breaker is still present, and approach the bandaging of the char above; then it holds more than previously, and increases its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb becomes dry more than what is necessary, then rub it with hot, sharp tea every time you remove it, and this should be every day, and loosen a little bit of the bandage; by this method, therefore, it cures the necrosis in the limb, and quickly repairs what the foolish ones do, which torture the member: it is bad, and if these are not done carefully, and I see no other thing than the worsening and the wrong doing.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breaking are, and diverse figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by percussion of the spear, and the collarbone fractures the entire bone just below the shoulder, as is done with a hatch or a fust; and because of this, this type of break is called «hatchure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above, perforating it, and this type of break is called «absolute»; and the wound of these two breaks is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion embedded, or a cut from the edge of the spear, or from falling on the stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If he has a fracture that pierces through, approaching the thread that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is healed into the bone as subtly as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called this "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by being hit by an arrow, or by falling, or by something similar, and the piece of the bone goes down below, and the threads are like those that they make in a cauldron when they hammer on them; then the arrow goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are those who have more than just moist bones, such as a child's skull; and they have all these methods of breaking, so that small pieces are removed like these; and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all methods of breaking by the removal above them, and the inquiry with tents, and the rotten charcoal that is above.
