And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large members, do not remove it, because many times death comes, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the sudden which come to the soldering
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the broken bone, especially when it is near the joint, and the unfortunate thing is to see the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot do the limbs its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care if it is fresh: if you administer stanching medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acacia, and similar things, so that you do not use any of these or all together, and mix with stanching wine or abundant oil or vinegar; and put it on the nose in a cloth, and hold it firmly, and do not let it out in the hand for a while; then remove it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you hold a piece of bread well made; because the property of the bread is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling is already hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the cover is on top, and make the excess apparent; or you cut it with any razor, until it is removed, and care until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is weakened after the injury
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains weak and thin afterward, this can be due to many causes: because it was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and could not come to the proper alignment of the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too large movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and rest; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great alignment, and the inflammation often of high heat, until the alignment comes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, it does not matter if its original appearance is lost: thus one should not believe those who say that the limb must be broken all over again, and many have done this in our land; and such practices are blamed, and great harms come from it, and perhaps death; however, if the fractures and twists are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs that are boiled, such as willow bark, roots, and marshmallow, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as good-quality honey, and you take the muscavend powder of willow bark, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take figs, and grind them with flour of coltsfoot, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the joint frozen due to continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you should move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awakened and hardened, as with a stone, and it needs to be frozen with ice, if it is necessary to cover it with the bone, with a slight and delicate incision; and put on a bandage and rest in treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be brought back towards the shoulder.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the shoulder swells, and if by chance it is reset, it may move in the wrong direction: many times it causes spasms and other pains; therefore, when this happens, first treat the injury, then let the limb rest until the abscess is calmed; then raise the member with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each member as it comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from the neck downwards.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the mandibles are dislocated and the dislocations of them occur in two ways: either they are slightly misaligned from their place and slightly softened; or they are completely displaced, hanging downwards, and tear the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and it covers its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its place in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is completely and accomplished, then you must quickly reset it, and do not delay; and in such a way that the healer pours the painful part of the dislocation into a small bowl of one of its hands at the root of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is outside, to hold even; and commands the patient to soften, his mandibles, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And when the dislocated joint is evened out, it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is painful to reset, especially when both mandibles are together, and the joints are heated with hot oil and oil, do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are evened out and the jaw with pain is closed properly to soften, place a cloth moistened in a cerote made of red oil and wax over it, then tie it lightly with soft bands; let the patient lie on their back, and their heads between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor make any effort to move, but take light food, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want lightly, and do not force them to open their mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour, and they are not converted back to their original shape, then fevers and sores may occur, and possibly diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is certain death; and often those who have had this die within fourteen days.
de la forcelle	of the forearm
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forearm cannot be dislocated from the side of the body without the use of force, and it is not reset once displaced, and one can feel it clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on their back, and extend their arms; then press the joint firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it; if the patient cannot be dislocated, and if it does not reset, then reset the joint as we have described; then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same is done for the shoulder, when it is released from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder can dislocate: one is that it dislocates to the side of the armpit; the second is to the back; and thirdly, it dislocates above, but this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside through the nerves; and many times it dislocates to the side, especially to those who have little flesh, for to these it must be done harshly; to those who have enough flesh, it must be done gently, and returned gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, hammering or crushing, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess, and thinks it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must examine him, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is turned towards the shoulder, and sets apart the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their differences manifest; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder, the top of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and the evil cannot bring its hand to its neck, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated high, if it is not hidden, because you will see it manifestly at the back; and this manner of dislocation is only to be returned, when it is new, or if the evil is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healers gently lift the bad joint up, then place their fingers below the joint, and push the joint back into place from above; and the healers gently lift and extend the arm upwards, then put it back down; it will quickly return.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come back as we have said, then it is necessary that the bad joint be soaked in hot water; and the healer applies a warming and soothing lotion, such as a decoction of aloe, fenugreek, and melilot in hot water, and it is applied; then the bad joint is placed on its back, and a cloth of even linen, neither too soft nor too hard, is placed below the joint, then the foot of the injured person is placed on the cloth, and the healer gently lifts the shoulder joint; another healer wets the head of the bad joint, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now completely back in place, and you must make sure that the person who is helping is larger than the bad joint; and they should be standing to the side of the body, and pulling the shoulder away from the bad joint, and lifting the joint upwards, so that the bad joint hangs in the air; and another healer takes the hand of the injured person down towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the pain is too light, nothing heavy can be done with it, and the dislocation now returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is done in another way: and it is that one places a long, thin twig in the earth, which the patient should also hold like a pistol, but not too heavy or too rough; then it is placed away from the painful part, but with a soft cloth over it, and the joint should be stretched out along the length of the bast; then the hand is placed on the other side firmly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a twig of two arms in width and four fingers in height, which has the head rounded to enter into the mouth from outside the jaw, like this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie a soft cloth above the injured shoulder, which was not bleeding, then remove it from the painful area; extend one arm over the long one, and tie the dislocation on the long arm, and the hand at the head of the hand, then put the arm over the broad end of an arrow, and stretch the hand down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is healed in any way, it is necessary to place a soft cloth of equal linen over the shoulder, then apply the poultice with powder from the mill, with incense and some honey, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the poultice from the shoulder evenly, and return the limb to the poultice, and embrace the hand at the neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move it little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; then move it more after four or seven days, and if it is stiff and does not become soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong and has come out due to moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauteries at three points, as it is placed before or in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot be raised above the arm, then cut or stretch or soften the nerve at the head of the shoulder; and cut or stretch or soften the joint so that it never returns to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is above the knees and the buttocks, or below, is caused by impulse and stretching of the hands, and it is treated with another oil; and it is cured until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes stiff and moves slowly, then use the hairs many times in a bath until the stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and repeatedly returns; and it has been dislocated in all parts, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not yet healed, for it can be seen and felt well; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is cut, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as possible when the joint is open, for if the joint is open and comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset completely at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, but causes more great pain, and perhaps it causes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to both hands; and his arms are spread, and the hands of the mirror like the shoulder on each side, in and out, and push the joint to its tendons together, or to the root of his palm, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the joint, then apply strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and tie it with two ministers, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when he sees the joint at his hand, if any oil is used to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as long as it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and press it together, and put the arm against the bad shoulder, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then release the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold well, then begin the bandaging and the limb again, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If it feels stiff after the resetting of the joint and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or place a piece of fat mutton grease on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and put in warm water; when it sweats, rub the joint immediately, then place the grease back on, and put in warm water again; do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then place a piece of moist, hot fat with butter on it, and press it; it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it should be quickly reset to its place as soon as it is dislocated, whether the fingers are swollen or if there is an abscess forming.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the hand on a table, extending the fingers of the hand, and aligning the palm so that it lies over the appearance of the joint, and holding it there until it is fully reset; then you should check if it is properly reset. Therefore, place the fingers on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's hand on their back, and the other person puts their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; if not, apply calming plasters and let it rest until you can begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If it cannot be suffered, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not attempt to straighten any part of the body until the hand is washed, and nothing can be strained: then cut the tendons or artery; if there is no other means but to straighten by cautery through the skin, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have said above it, then strain and leave it for 4 days, then remove and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no swelling, then pour boiling water on it, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Fingers are not dislocated at each part of the hand, neither at the back of the palm or the belly; then hold the finger, and reset the dislocation to your fist as it returns, then support the tip of the finger, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then put it in place that day; and bind it as we have said, and remove the bandage each day, and move it, and rejoin it; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	backwards dislocation of the shoulder joint
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck joint is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the dislocation suddenly moves without volition, cannot be held, and often softens any member, or the two shoulders or both arms or one; and often the shoulder moves at an angle of 90 degrees; this is called "gibbosity": the cure is to reward the gibbosity if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the entire time.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or from percussions or similar things, they said in the old ways of healing with great words, but I have abbreviated them according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of the splint that comes to the front of the leg, there is no engineering or healing; and so with the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure it except by the proper one that comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched out over his face in a straight line, and he should have some strain outside of him, so that he does not become bloated; then make the bandage at the top on the ground in a firm way, and the other at the bottom, and tie one ligature outside of the hairs of the wound, and the other around the buttocks, and as the hips, and as the knees; and two assistants should secure the ligatures, one at the top and the others at the bottom, among the two bandages; and they should be well fastened, the bandage as we have said, and the poultice put its palms on the spine in a firm way, until it regains.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a table of three arms' length, and bend it away from the body, and the painful parts be on the side, and press the head of the table away from the body, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and put the mirrors his feet on the other head of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the twisted one who turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fasten two ropes to the head of the painful arm of a long arm, and on the side of the feet two others, and between each rope, outside and inside, one span of length; and in each rope there is one knot, or the twisted one corrects it, and the ropes are firmly on the ground so that they do not move; and between each two ropes there is one rope turning, following the direction of the turned ones, and there are two small ropes of a span of length to turn the twisted one; then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the twisted one at the head, and the other ligament to the feet on the other twisted one, and each minister turns his turned one to all the ligament, and the masters put the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a drying plaster with an abundance of honey, and then soak, and then place the leg on a tablet of three fingers in length, which supports the neck of the spine and the part of the spine that is healthy, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of health, then medicines must be administered that are softening and soothing, with the method that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never come to appear in the back spine of the back, and it is the bone that opens, for which we should not have any presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder do not come out only as dislocations, but not so much like other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than that, and slightly dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of dislocations inside is such that when one leg with a bad joint is joined with a healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy ones, and cannot double its knee to the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen with abscesses, because the cause of the belly comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes to this deficiency is that these accidents are contrary to those previously mentioned.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has this before are that they stand well on their leg according to completion; however, they do not double over with pain in the groin, and if you want to make them walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and swell the ankle, and when they walk, they pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has this behind are that they cannot spread their groin, or double over, and the other leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated at the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are that you will know when the dislocation is old, and it will remain according to its position, if there is no cure; and there is no need for it to be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four types of dislocation, you must quickly return the joint, extend and flex it, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you apply strong pressure, and extend the leg firmly to two fingers, or one finger that is tied above the knee; and other ministers extend their hand under the tail in a similar manner as they bite their hands from their sockets, then squeeze the neck of the limb; and others grip the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat its similarity. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to support the misaligned limb on its healthy side, then place the arm over the root of the neck, and the arm that is outside the shoulder, then extend the arm above the shoulder and towards the armpit; then take other ministers to grasp the large arm of the shoulder misalignment, and extend it back into place: it will return to its limb now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot hold the two affected feet together with a strong sinew above the two heels, and above the two ankles, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers more than the other; then it should be suspended above the head on a stick, and the other arm should be stretched out below the earth; then command the minister to embrace the neck of the back, and another minister should hang with the affected limb, who should embrace the back properly, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is gone, bend the affected limbs as we have described in the case of gout, and stretch the sinew properly above the affected leg and on the foot; then place two ties, one at the head and the other at the foot, then fold the tie between the backbones in the form of the dislocation; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not become stiff, then extend each minister towards him, and the patient put equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the flat table, and press it as we have said in the gangrene, and cut off the bad parts on the clean side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the bad leg strongly, as I have said; and place the remedy for pain above the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the bad leg downwards, nor to lift it up, but it should be as it was when the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have said about lying on the two hips; and it should be on its face, and the hamstring extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint on the table; and it will be good when the bad legs extend their legs, and they will be even; then support the knees, and put the plaster, and the bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, remove the bandage, and let it walk slowly, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, from within and without, and from behind; but it does not dislocate from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he cannot do so at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if possible, and put your back against his face, and put your foot on his; then take his shoulder to your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder well; and other ministers extend his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can lightly bend his leg at the knee; and put the plaster on, and let the leg and knee cool together for three or four hours, then remove it; and do not work on the patient again until his members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the members are not in place, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are aligned.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never sprained and never fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is dislocated, and it can be felt before at the part where it is dislocated: the symptoms are slight, and one should gently extend it slightly to the hands when it is sprained only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold the painful part with your hands, above the ankle; then take the bone to your right hand, and then to your left twice, then extend it upwards, and strike it well in the upper part; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and taking the bone; if it returns, it is good; if not, if you repeat the work, it will return; and if it cannot return like this, you should make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly fix the bone between their legs, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not dislocate; then hold the painful part with your hand, and another minister extends the bone to their hands or to the ligament, where they tie it above the bone; then extend all the ministers equally, and the cloths should be between the legs of the patient to hold the bone when you are extending it; then put the patient's hands even with the dislocation, and another minister holds the leg straight at the side, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she goes to the point, if she puts the plaster and wipes it above, and the strain forms, and ties the foot to the leg, and holds the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the limbs are not too stretched; then leaves her for two or three days, and if the limbs are not straight, then the plaster; then releases her on the third or fourth day, and allows her to walk the injured part for four days; and if she goes before this term, it is not safe that it does not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you relieve it as we have said in another place, until it is healthy.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they need to be extended, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the shoulder or the arm, it is necessary to make the patient sit with their bad arm straight out or on a table, and put your hand on what opens these joints, then press firmly on your hand until it regains its place; and when it is even, and there is no opening, put the sole of your foot on the patient's shoulder, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often the pain is fatal: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and do not know the art well, and have not used it long, and are not merciful and slow, and hardhearted; at the beginning of things, gently treat the abscess, and leave the pain in God's hands, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place, as soon as the abscesses have subsided; and when the member is in place, administer gentle treatment for healing, as is appropriate, from time to time; and if with dislocation there is fracture, and small bones are broken, remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
